Commentary
This passage is an extended discussion on the definition of fiqh, defending it against objections and clarifying the status of the muqallid. The author begins by reiterating that fiqh is a firmly rooted faculty (malakah) for deriving all shar'i rulings, not actual knowledge of every ruling. This distinction is crucial: a faqih may not know every ruling at all times due to obstacles like conflicting evidence or personal limitations, but the capacity to derive remains. The response to the first objection clarifies that 'knowledge' in the definition refers to this malakah, not actual knowledge. The critique from Sharh al-Tanqih is answered by stating that the readiness (tahiyyah) is neither near nor far but the innate ability to derive all rulings. The second objection concerns the term 'evidences' (adillah). The author explains that in the definition, 'evidences' means indicators (amarat) that lead the mujtahid to certain knowledge of the obligation to act. This is exclusive to the mujtahid by consensus; the muqallid does not attain such certainty through speculation. Thus the muqallid is excluded. A doubt is then raised: if the muqallid relies on the mujtahid, doesn't he too have certain knowledge? The answer is that the muqallid's certainty is not based on speculation but on the mujtahid's statement, which is not a detailed evidence. Therefore, the muqallid is outside the definition. Finally, the author refutes Amanullah Banarasi who equated the muqallid's and mujtahid's positions. The author insists on the difference: the mujtahid's speculation binds only him, not the muqallid, due to two separate consensuses. The muqallid acts based on the mujtahid's statement, not the speculation itself.

Key Terms
فقہ (fiqh): A firmly rooted malakah for deriving all shar'i rulings from detailed evidences.
ملکہ (malakah): A firmly rooted quality or faculty in the soul enabling the derivation of rulings.
مقلد (muqallid): One who follows a mujtahid without independent inquiry; his basis is the mujtahid's statement, not his own speculation.
امارات (amarat): Indicators that lead to knowledge of the obligation to act; they produce certainty in the mujtahid by consensus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is a muqallid not considered a faqih?
A) Because a muqallid does not know all the rulings.
B) Because a muqallid's knowledge is based on the mujtahid's statement, not on detailed evidences.
C) Because a muqallid cannot understand Arabic.
D) Because a muqallid's speculation is not binding on him.

Key Takeaway
Fiqh is a faculty of derivation, not mere knowledge; a muqallid, lacking this faculty and relying on the mujtahid's statement, is not a faqih.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Resolving the Objection: Fiqh as Knowledge of the Obligation to Act
Resolving a logical objection to the definition of fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why defining fiqh as 'knowledge of the obligation to act' is a valid rasm (descriptive definition) using a lazim (necessary consequence), and not a change in meaning.

Core Idea
The definition using obligation-to-act is a valid rasm via lazim, not a reduction.

This passage addresses a subtle objection that arose from the earlier answer that 'evidences' in the definition of fiqh mean 'indicators' (amarat). If indicators lead to knowledge of the obligation to act, then the definition becomes 'knowledge of the obligation to act', restricting fiqh to only the category of obligation. The author resolves this by clarifying that the definition is a rasm (descriptive definition) that uses a necessary consequence (lazim) of knowing the rulings, namely that one must act upon them. This does not change the essential meaning but highlights a necessary implication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objection arises from the second answer: if 'evidences' means 'amarat' (indicators) that lead to knowledge of the obligation to act, then the definition 'knowledge of the rulings from detailed evidences' would become 'knowledge of the obligation to act on the rulings'.
This would exclude rulings like prohibition, recommendation, etc.
2
Trace the logical consequence
If fiqh is defined as 'knowledge of the obligation to act', then only rulings of obligation (wujub) would be included, not the other four categories (haram, nadb, ibaha, karaha). This contradicts the usage of the fuqaha.
The objection is that the definition becomes too narrow.
3
Locate the author's resolution
The author says 'except that it could be said that it is a rasm, and therefore it is permissible to use the necessary consequence (lazim).' He explains that the definition is not a hadd (essential definition) but a rasm (descriptive definition), and a rasm can be given using a lazim.
The lazim of knowing the rulings is the obligation to act upon them.
4
Apply the concept of rasm and lazim
Since knowing shar'i rulings necessarily implies that one must act on them, using 'knowledge of the obligation to act' as a definition is valid for a rasm. It does not change the meaning but highlights a necessary consequence.
This preserves the full scope of fiqh (five categories).
5
Verify with the legal definition dissector
The legal_definition_dissector for fiqh shows its mahall is the mujtahid, sabab is ijtihad, shart is detailed evidences, and athar is acting on rulings. The lazim (acting on rulings) is a consequence, not the essence.

قوله - نعم يلزم أن يكون عبارة عن العلم الخ فقہ کی تعریف مشہور کی جامعیت و مانعیت پر جو دواعتراضات وارد ہوئے تھے دونوں کا جواب مصنف نے دے دیا تھا۔ اول کا جواب لان المراد المملکۃ اور دوم کا جواب لان المراد بالا دلہ الامارات سے دیا لیکن اعتراض دوم کے جواب پر ایک اشکال لازم آتا ہے اس اشکال کو مصنف نے اپنے قول نعم ملزم ان یکون الخ سے بیان کیا ہے۔ اشکال کی تقریر : اعتراض دوم کے جواب کی تقریر سے واضح ہے کہ ادلہ سے امارات مراد ہیں اور امارات اس ظن کا افادہ کرتا ہے جو مجتہد کو وجوب العمل بالا حکام کے علم تک پہونچاتا ہے مگر اس سے یہ لازم آ رہا ہے کہ تعریف فقہ میں اعلم بالا حکام سے العلم بوجوب العمل بالا حکام مراد ہو کیونکہ آپ نے ادلہ سے امارات مراد لیا ہے کہ امارات وجوب العمل بالا حکام کے علم تک مفضی ہوتا ہے۔ اس تقدیر پر فقہ علم بالا حکام کا نام نہیں رہجائے گا بلکہ فقہ، العلم بوجوب العمل بالا حکام کا نام ہو جائے گا پس وجوب صوم وصلوۃ، حرمت زنا و شرب خمر وغیرہ احکام فقہ میں داخل نہ رہیں گے بلکہ ان احکام پر عمل کے علم ہونے کا نام فقہ قرار پائے گا حالانکہ یہ تصریحات فقہاء کے خلاف ہے کیونکہ فقہ تو نفس احکام کے علم کا نام ہے ان احکام پر عمل کے واجب ہونے کے علم نام نہیں۔ علاوہ ازیں اعلم بالا حکام سے اعلم بوجوب العمل بالا حکام مراد لینے پر فقہ اپنے اقسام خمسہ یعنی وجوب، حرمت، ندب، اباحت اور کراہت میں سے صرف اور صرف ایک قسم وجوب پر محدود و منحصر ہوکر رہے گا حالانکہ فقہ کا اطلاق احکام کے اقسام خمسہ پر ہوتا ہے۔ قوله الا أن يقال انه رسم فيجوز باللازم اس عبارت میں اعتراض مذکور کا جواب مسطور ہے جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ در حقیقت فقہ تو علم احکام ہی کا نام ہے مگر علم بوجوب العمل بالا حکام سے اس لئے تعبیر کیا جارہاہے کہ علم احکام کے لئے علم وجوب عمل لازم ہے۔ چونکہ یہ تعریف حدی نہیں ہے بلکہ رسی ہے اور شیء کی تعریف رسمی اس کے لازم سے صحیح ہوتی ہے چنانچہ یہ ظاہر ہے کہ احکام شرعیہ کے جانے کالازمہ اس پر عمل کرتا ہے بنابر ایں
His statement: 'Yes, it necessarily implies that it is an expression for knowledge...' The author had already answered the two objections concerning the comprehensiveness and exclusiveness of the famous definition of fiqh. The first answer was 'because by it is meant the faculty (al-malaka),' and the second answer was 'because by the evidences are meant the indicators (amarat).' But on the answer to the second objection, a difficulty necessarily arises. The author expressed this difficulty with his statement 'Yes, it necessarily implies that it is...' The explanation of the difficulty: From the explanation of the answer to the second objection, it is clear that by 'evidences' are meant 'amarat' (indicators), and 'amarat' produce conjecture (zann) which leads the mujtahid to knowledge of the obligation to act on the rulings. But from this it necessarily follows that in the definition of fiqh, 'knowledge of the rulings' means 'knowledge of the obligation to act on the rulings', because you have taken 'evidences' to mean 'amarat' that lead to knowledge of the obligation to act on the rulings. On this assumption, fiqh will no longer be called knowledge of the rulings, but rather fiqh will be called knowledge of the obligation to act on the rulings. Thus, the obligation of fasting, prayer, prohibition of adultery, drinking wine, etc., will not be included in fiqh; instead, fiqh will be defined as knowledge of acting upon these rulings, even though this contradicts the explicit statements of the fuqaha, because fiqh is the name of knowledge of the rulings themselves, not knowledge of the obligation to act upon them. Moreover, taking 'knowledge of the rulings' as 'knowledge of the obligation to act on the rulings' will restrict fiqh to only one of the five categories—namely obligation (wujub)—whereas fiqh applies to all five categories: obligation, prohibition, recommendation, permissibility, and dislike. His statement: 'Except that it could be said that it is a rasm (descriptive definition), and therefore it is permissible to use the necessary consequence (lazim).' In this statement, the answer to the mentioned objection is recorded. The summary of the answer is that in reality, fiqh is the name of knowledge of the rulings, but it is expressed as 'knowledge of the obligation to act on the rulings' because knowledge of the rulings necessarily implies knowledge of the obligation to act. Since this definition is not a hadd (essential definition) but a rasm (descriptive definition), and a rasm of something is validly given using its necessary consequence (lazim), accordingly, it is obvious that the necessary consequence of knowing the shar'i rulings is acting upon them. Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage addresses a problem arising from the earlier answer that 'evidences' in the definition of fiqh means 'indicators' (amarat). If the definition is 'knowledge of the rulings from detailed evidences' and those evidences are indicators that lead the mujtahid to knowledge of the obligation to act, then the definition effectively becomes 'knowledge of the obligation to act on rulings', not 'knowledge of the rulings'. This would restrict fiqh to only the category of obligation (wujub), excluding prohibition, recommendation, etc. The author resolves this by clarifying that this definition is a rasm (descriptive definition) that uses a necessary consequence (lazim). Since knowing the rulings necessarily implies knowing that one should act on them, expressing the definition via the necessary consequence is valid for a rasm. Thus, the definition does not actually change the meaning; it merely highlights a necessary implication.

Key Terms
رسم (rasm): A descriptive definition using a necessary property or consequence, not the essence.
لازم (lazim): A necessary consequence that flows from the essence of the thing defined.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does the author resolve the objection that the definition restricts fiqh to the category of obligation?
A) By redefining the term 'fiqh'.
B) By asserting that the definition is a hadd (essential definition).
C) By explaining that the definition is a rasm (descriptive) and using a necessary consequence is permissible.
D) By denying that the objection arises.

Key Takeaway
A definition that uses a necessary consequence (lazim) is valid as a rasm, preserving the full scope of the defined term.

Defining Fiqh as 'Ilm: Objections and Responses
Refuting objections that fiqh cannot be called 'ilm because it includes speculative rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi definition of fiqh as 'ilm and refute the objection that speculative rulings exclude fiqh from being 'ilm using the two responses from the passage.

Core Idea
Fiqh is 'ilm: the mujtahid's knowledge of speculative rulings becomes certain through definitive obligation and consensus.

This passage addresses a key objection to the Hanafi definition of fiqh as 'ilm (knowledge). Critics argue that most fiqh rulings are based on speculative evidence (zanniyat) like qiyas and khabar wahid, so fiqh cannot be called certain knowledge. The author provides two sophisticated responses: first, the mujtahid attains certain knowledge due to definitive obligation and consensus; second, 'ilm can be used in a general sense encompassing both certainty and speculation. Understanding this defence is crucial for grasping the epistemological foundation of Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two senses of 'ilm
Recognise that in the passage, 'ilm is used in two ways: (1) firm belief and certainty (i'tiqad jazim), and (2) a general meaning that includes both certainty and speculation.
The second sense is key to the second response.
2
Trace the objection
Understand that if 'ilm is restricted to certain belief, then speculative rulings would be excluded from fiqh, rendering the definition problematic.
The objection is that most fiqh rulings are based on zanni evidence.
3
Analyse the first response
Study the argument that for the mujtahid, speculative rulings become certain knowledge because acting upon them is definitively obligatory (wujub al-'amal qat'an), and there is a definitive consensus (ijma qati') that the mujtahid's knowledge is certain.
This response relies on the authority of consensus.
4
Analyse the second response
Examine the alternative defence: the term 'ilm in the definition can be taken in its broader sense that includes both certain and speculative matters, thereby avoiding exclusion.
This appeals to linguistic flexibility.
5
Evaluate the evidence
Confirm that both responses are supported by textual evidence: the first by a definitive consensus, the second by the usage of the early scholars (qudama').
The Sharh al-Minhaj quote reinforces the first response.

قوله من ههنا علمت اندفاع ماقيل الفقه من باب الظنون الخ اس عبارت سے ایک اعتراض پھر اس کے جواب کی طرف اشارہ ہے قوم نے فقہ کی تعریف جو اعلم سے کی ہے اس پر اعتراض ہے کہ العلم" سے فقہ کی تعریف کرنا صحیح نہیں ورنہ فقہ کا ، متد بہ حصہ جیسے قیاس خبر واحد اور اجماع منقول عن الواحد فقہ سے خارج ہو جائے گا کیونکہ علم اعتقاد جازم اور یقین کامل کا نام ہے اور جبکہ فقہ کے اکثر مسائل قیاس ، خبر واحد اور اجماعات منقولہ سے ثابت ہیں اور سب از قبیل ظنیات ہیں پس جو از قبیل ظنیات ہیں وہ فقہ میں کیونکر داخل ہوں گے جس کو علم یعنی اعتقاد جازم سے مقید کر دیا گیا ہے۔ جواب :۔ اس کا جواب ما سبق میں گذر چکا اور وہ یہ ہے کہ فقہ وجوب عمل بالا حکام کے علم سے عبارت ہے اور اسطرح کا علم بذریعہ امارات مجتہد ہی کو حاصل ہوتا ہے پھر یہ احکام گر چه ادلہ ظنیہ خبر واحد، قیاس اور اجماع آحادی سے ثابت ہوتے ہیں مگر حضرات مجتہدین کو ادلہ ظنیہ سے ثابت شدہ احکام کا علم یقینی قطعی حاصل ہوتا ہے کیونکہ اجماع قطعی سے یہ امر حق ہے کہ مجتہد کا عل علم یقینی قطعی ہے لہذا فقہ کوعلم کہنا صحیح ہے۔ اور ظنیات کا فقہ سے خروج نہ ہوگا۔
جواب مذکور سے ملتا جلتا جواب شرح منھاج میں بھی دیا گیا ہے۔ اور وہ یہ ہے۔
الحكم المظنون للمجتهد يجب العمل به قطعا للدليل القاطع وكل حكم يجب العمل به قطعا علم قطعا انه حكم الله تعالى والالم يجب العمل به كل ما علم قطعاً انه حكم الله تعالى فهو معلوم قطعا فالحكم المظنون للمجتهد معلوم قطعا فالفقه علم قطعى والظن وسيلة اليه"۔
یعنی مجتہد کے حکم مظنون پر دلیل قاطع کی وجہ سے عمل کرنا قطعی طور پر واجب ہے اور وہ حکم جس پر قطعی طور پر عمل کرنا واجب ہو اس کے بارے میں بالیقین معلوم ہے کہ وہ اللہ تعالیٰ کا حکم ہے ورنہ اس پر عمل ہی واجب نہ ہوتا اور ہر وہ حکم جس کا حکم الہی ہونا قطعی طور پر معلوم ہو وہ معلوم قطعی ہے لہذا مجتہد کا مظنون معلوم قطعی ہے اور فقہ علم قطعی ہے رہاظن تو اس تک وسیلہ ہے۔
قوله على أن العلم حقيقة فيما ليس بتصور ايضاً اعتراض سابق کہ فقہ کی تعریف علم سے کر نا صحیح نہیں" کا دوسرا جواب ہے۔
جواب : کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ علم صرف یقین اور اعتقاد جازم ہی کو نہیں کہتے بلکہ علم کا اطلاق دو معنوں پر ہوتا ہے ایک یقین و اعتقاد جازم پر دوسرا غیر تصویر پر اور دوسرا معنی ایسا عام ہے جو اعتقاد جازم اور ظن دونوں کو عام ہے پس فقہ کی تعریف میں جو علم مذکور ہے اس سے علم کا یہی معنی عام مراد ہے تا کہ یقینی وظنی دونوں کو شامل ہو جائے اور فقہ کا صرف قطعی ہونا یا فقہ سے خنیات [ظنیات؟] کا خارج ہونا نہ لا زم آئے۔
The obligation to act became necessary for knowledge of legal rulings. Therefore, it will not be necessary that the obligation of fasting and prayer and the prohibition of adultery, wine drinking, etc., remain in fiqh. However, if this definition were a real definition (haddi), the objection would be valid. His statement 'fihi ma fihi' indicates the weakness of the above answer. The reason for weakness is that while it is correct that a formal definition (rasmi) by a necessary property (lazim) is valid, but absolutely, defining a thing by any necessary property (whether predicable necessary property or essential necessary property) is not correct. Rather, defining a thing by that necessary property which is predicated on its subject, i.e., of the category of predicable necessary properties, is valid. In this context, although the knowledge of the obligation to act is a necessary property of knowledge of rulings, nevertheless this necessary property (obligation to act) is not predicated on its subject (knowledge of rulings), because it is not said that 'knowledge of the obligation to act is called knowledge of rulings.' In short, the knowledge of the obligation of rulings is of the category of essential necessary properties for knowledge of rulings. Therefore, definition by this necessary property is not valid. The author alluded to this meaning in his gloss. Indication that it is a necessary property by way of existence, so it is not predicated, thus it does not make a definer. Answer: This is that definition by a separate (mubayin) thing is also permissible, as narrated from the early scholars. Accordingly, the early scholars felt no hesitation in mentioning separate items in definitions. Hence, although the obligation to act is not predicated on knowledge of rulings because it is separate, nevertheless definition by it is correct based on the school of the early scholars. His statement 'min huna 'alimta indifa'a ma qila al-fiqh min bab al-zunun' etc. This phrase indicates an objection and then its answer. The people objected to the definition of fiqh by 'ilm: that defining fiqh by 'ilm is not correct, otherwise the sound part of fiqh, like qiyas, khabar wahid, and ijma manqul 'an al-wahid, would exit from fiqh, because 'ilm is firm belief and complete certainty, whereas most issues of fiqh are proven by qiyas, khabar wahid, and transmitted ijma'at, and all are of the category of speculative matters. So how can speculative matters enter into fiqh, which has been restricted to 'ilm meaning firm belief? Answer: The answer has already preceded, and it is that fiqh is the knowledge of rulings with the obligation to act, and such knowledge is obtained by the mujtahid through evidence. Then these rulings, even if established by speculative evidence like khabar wahid, qiyas, and non-mass-transmitted ijma, nevertheless the mujtahids obtain certain and definitive knowledge of rulings established by speculative evidence, because it is a definitive consensus (ijma 'qati) that the knowledge of the mujtahid is certain and definitive. Therefore, calling fiqh 'ilm is correct. And speculative matters will not exit from fiqh. A similar answer is given in Sharh al-Minhaj, and it is: The speculative ruling for the mujtahid: acting upon it is definitively obligatory due to a definitive proof. And every ruling that acting upon it is definitively obligatory, it is known with certainty that it is the ruling of Allah, otherwise acting upon it would not be obligatory. And every ruling that is known with certainty to be the ruling of Allah is definitively known. Therefore, the speculative ruling for the mujtahid is definitively known, so fiqh is definitive knowledge, and speculation is merely a means to it. His statement 'ala anna al-haqiqa fima laysa bi tasawwurin aydan' is a second answer to the previous objection that defining fiqh by 'ilm is not correct. The gist of the answer is that 'ilm is not only certainty and firm belief; rather, 'ilm is applied to two meanings: one is certainty and firm belief, the second is non-conceptual. And the second meaning is general, encompassing both firm belief and speculation. So in the definition of fiqh, the word 'ilm refers to this general meaning, so that both certain and speculative matters are included, and it does not necessitate that fiqh is only definitive or that speculative matters exit from fiqh.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This is a discussion of objections to defining fiqh as 'ilm (knowledge). The author first addresses the objection that using 'wujub al-'amal' (obligation to act) as a necessary property (lazim) is invalid because it is not predicated (mahmul) on the subject (knowledge of rulings). He responds that definition by a separate (mubayin) property is allowed according to the early scholars. Then a second objection is raised: that most fiqh rulings are based on speculative evidence (zanniyat) like qiyas and khabar wahid, so defining fiqh as 'ilm (certain knowledge) would exclude them. The response is twofold: first, for the mujtahid, these rulings become certain knowledge due to a definitive consensus that the mujtahid's knowledge is certain; second, 'ilm can be used in a general sense that includes both certainty and speculation. The author quotes a passage from Sharh al-Minhaj to support the first response. The discussion is based on Hanafi usul, where the certainty of the mujtahid's knowledge is defended by the definitive obligation to act based on speculative evidence.

Key Terms
العلم (al-‘ilm): In this passage, 'ilm is taken in two senses: (1) firm belief and certainty (i‘tiqad jazim), and (2) a general meaning that includes both certainty and speculation.
الظن (al-zann): Speculative belief that falls short of certainty; rulings based on qiyas, khabar wahid, and non-mass-transmitted ijma are considered zanni.
القطع (al-qat‘): Definitive certainty; the mujtahid's knowledge of rulings is considered qat‘i even if derived from zanni evidence, because of the decisive proof (dalil qati‘) requiring action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it correct to define fiqh as 'ilm (knowledge) despite many rulings being based on speculative evidence?
A) Because 'ilm is defined only as certainty, and speculative rulings are not part of fiqh.
B) Because the mujtahid obtains certain knowledge of these rulings due to the definitive obligation to act and the consensus that his knowledge is certain.
C) Because 'ilm in Arabic always includes speculation.
D) Because the early scholars rejected the use of speculative evidence in fiqh.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defends the definition of fiqh as 'ilm by arguing that the mujtahid's knowledge from speculative evidence is certain, either through definitive obligation and consensus or through a broader sense of the term 'ilm.

The Alternative Definition of Fiqh and Its Critique
Alternative definition of fiqh and its critique

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the alternative definition of fiqh that limits it to definitive rulings, explain why Muslim al-Thubut rejects it, and state the implication for the scope of Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
To define fiqh as only definitive rulings would exclude most of fiqh, since most evidence is speculative.

In this passage from Muslim al-Thubut, we encounter a proposed definition of fiqh that seems rigorous but ultimately unworkable. The text argues that limiting fiqh to definitive rulings would cut out the vast majority of actual fiqh issues, because most rulings in the Hanafi school are based on speculative (zanni) evidence. The author considers this view far-fetched.

Guided Path
1
State the alternative definition
Identify the two components of the proposed definition: knowledge of definitive rulings (al-ahkam al-qat‘iyyah) and the faculty of deduction (malakat al-istinbat).
This definition aims for certainty in fiqh.
2
Understand the critique
The author points out that this definition would exclude all issues established by speculative (zanni) evidence. Since most hadith are ahad (speculative) and the mutawatir sunnah is very little, the vast majority of fiqh rulings would be excluded.
Consider the ratio of zanni to qat‘i evidence in the Hanafi school.
3
Grasp the author's conclusion
The author dismisses the definition as 'very far-fetched' (ba‘id jiddan), especially the addition of 'action' (al-‘amal) to the definition by some teachers.
The key is that fiqh must accommodate zanni evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعضهم جعل الفقه عبارة عن العلم بالاحكام القطعية مع ملكة الاستنباط ويلزم عليه خروج المسائل الثابتة بالادلة الظنية وهي كثيرة الاترى أن السنة المتواترة قليلة جدا والتزام ذالك بلالزوم وجعل العمل داخلا في تحديد هذا العلم كما ذهب اليه بعض مشائخنا بعيد جداً
And some made fiqh an expression for knowledge of definitive rulings along with the faculty of deduction. And it would necessitate the exclusion of issues established by speculative evidence, which are many. Do you not see that the mutawatir sunnah is very little? And committing to that without necessity, and including action in the definition of this science as some of our teachers held, is very far-fetched.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This is the matn (core text) from Muslim al-Thubut. It presents an alternative definition of fiqh: knowledge of definitive (qat‘i) rulings along with the faculty of deduction (malakat al-istinbat). The author points out the problem: this definition would exclude most issues of fiqh that are based on speculative evidence (zanni), because such evidence does not produce definitive knowledge. He notes that mutawatir reports are very few, so most rulings would be excluded. The author finds this view far-fetched (ba‘id jiddan), especially the inclusion of 'action' (al-‘amal) in the definition, as some of their teachers held. This matn sets up the discussion for the commentary (sharh) that follows.

Key Terms
الاحكام القطعية (al-ahkam al-qat‘iyyah): Rulings that are definitively known, derived from certain evidence (like mutawatir hadith or clear Quranic text).
ملكة الاستنباط (malakat al-istinbat): The faculty or ability to deduce rulings from the sources; part of the definition proposed by some.
السنة المتواترة (al-sunnah al-mutawatirah): Mass-transmitted hadith that yields certain knowledge; noted as very little in quantity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn, what problem arises from defining fiqh as 'knowledge of definitive rulings'?
A) It includes action in the definition, which is unnecessary.
B) It excludes the faculty of deduction.
C) It excludes many issues based on speculative evidence, which are numerous because mutawatir evidence is scarce.
D) It makes fiqh too broad.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines fiqh as knowledge of practical legal rulings derived from detailed evidence, both definitive and speculative; restricting it to definitive rulings is rejected as too narrow.

Defending Fiqh as Certain Knowledge: Two Hanafi Responses
Refuting the claim that fiqh cannot be called 'ilm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how Hanafi usul defends fiqh as 'ilm (certain knowledge) despite its reliance on zanni evidences, using the concepts of ijma qat'i and the dual definition of 'ilm.

Core Idea
Fiqh is certain knowledge because the mujtahid must act on it definitively, and ijma confirms that.

A common objection holds that fiqh cannot be called 'ilm because many of its rulings are based on speculative (zanni) evidence such as khabar wahid and qiyas. The Hanafi school offers two powerful responses: first, that a qat'i ijma (consensus) makes the mujtahid's ruling certain in practice; second, that 'ilm in the definition of fiqh is used in a broad sense that includes both certain and speculative beliefs. This lesson unpacks both arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Understand the claim that fiqh is not 'ilm because it is derived from zanni (speculative) proofs, whereas 'ilm traditionally means certain, unquestionable knowledge.
The objection targets the epistemological status of fiqh, not its legal validity.
2
Analyze the first response: ijma qat'i
Examine the argument that a qat'i ijma (consensus) establishes that a mujtahid's rulings—even those from zanni evidences—are certain for him. The proof from Sharh Minhaj provides a syllogism: any ruling that must be acted upon qat'an is known qat'an to be Allah's ruling; thus the zanni ruling becomes certain.
The certainty arises from the obligation to act, not from the evidence itself.
3
Analyze the second response: dual definition of 'ilm
Explore the broader meaning of 'ilm that includes both yaqin (certain conviction) and the opposite of tasawwur (mental representation), i.e., any cognitive affirmation. The definition of fiqh uses 'ilm in this general sense to cover both qat'i and zanni rulings.
This refutes the objection by showing that 'ilm is not limited to certainty.
4
Synthesize the two responses
See how the two arguments work together: the first establishes the certainty of the ruling in practice, the second shows that even if one insists on certainty, the broader definition of 'ilm accommodates zann. Both preserve fiqh as 'ilm.
The combined force leaves no room for the objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور اجماع آحادی سے ثابت ہوتے ہیں مگر حضرات مجتہدین کو ادلہ ظنیہ سے ثابت شدہ احکام کا علم یقینی قطعی حاصل ہوتا ہے کیونکہ اجماع قطعی سے یہ امر حق ہے کہ مجتہد کا عل علم یقینی قطعی ہے لہذا فقہ کوعلم کہنا صحیح ہے۔ اور ظنیات کا فقہ سے خروج نہ ہوگا۔ جواب مذکور سے ملتا جلتا جواب شرح منھاج میں بھی دیا گیا ہے۔ اور وہ یہ ہے۔ الحكم المظنون للمجتهد يجب العمل به قطعا للدليل القاطع وكل حكم يجب العمل به قطعا علم قطعا انه حكم الله تعالى والالم يجب العمل به كل ما علم قطعاً انه حكم الله تعالى فهو معلوم قطعا فالحكم المظنون للمجتهد معلوم قطعا فالفقه علم قطعى والظن وسيلة اليه. یعنی مجتہد کے حکم مظنون پر دلیل قاطع کی وجہ سے عمل کرنا قطعی طور پر واجب ہے اور وہ حکم جس پر قطعی طور پر عمل کرنا واجب ہو اس کے بارے میں بالیقین معلوم ہے کہ وہ اللہ تعالیٰ کا حکم ہے ورنہ اس پر عمل ہی واجب نہ ہوتا اور ہر وہ حکم جس کا حکم الہی ہونا قطعی طور پر معلوم ہو وہ معلوم قطعی ہے لہذا مجتہد کا مظنون معلوم قطعی ہے اور فقہ علم قطعی ہے رہاظن تو اس تک وسیلہ ہے۔ قوله على أن العلم حقيقة فيما ليس بتصور ايضاً اعتراض سابق کہ فقہ کی تعریف علم سے کر نا صحیح نہیں“ کا دوسرا جواب ہے۔ جواب : کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ علم صرف یقین اور اعتقاد جازم ہی کو نہیں کہتے بلکہ علم کا اطلاق دو معنوں پر ہوتا ہے ایک یقین و اعتقاد جازم پر دوسرا غیر تصویر پر اور دوسرا معنی ایسا عام ہے جو اعتقاد جازم اور ظن دونوں کو عام ہے پس فقہ کی تعریف میں جو علم مذکور ہے اس سے علم کا یہی معنی عام مراد ہے تا کہ یقینی وظنی دونوں کو شامل ہو جائے اور فقہ کا صرف قطعی ہونا یا فقہ سے خنیات کا خارج ہونا نہ لا زم آئے۔
And they are established from ahad ijma, but the honorable mujtahidun obtain certain and qat'i knowledge of rulings established from zanni evidences because by qat'i ijma this matter is true: that the knowledge of a mujtahid is certain and qat'i. Therefore, calling fiqh 'ilm is correct. And zanniyat will not be excluded from fiqh. A similar response to the mentioned response is also given in Sharh Minhaj, and it is: 'The zanni ruling for the mujtahid must be acted upon qat'an due to the qat'i proof. And every ruling that must be acted upon qat'an is known qat'an that it is the ruling of Allah ta'ala; otherwise acting upon it would not be obligatory. And every ruling that is known qat'an to be the ruling of Allah ta'ala is known qat'an. So the zanni ruling for the mujtahid is known qat'an, so fiqh is qat'i knowledge, and zann is a means to it.' That is: acting upon the mujtahid's zanni ruling is qat'an obligatory due to the qat'i proof, and that ruling about which acting is qat'an obligatory is known with certainty that it is the ruling of Allah ta'ala; otherwise acting upon it would not be obligatory at all. And every ruling whose being Allah's ruling is known qat'an is known qat'an. Therefore the mujtahid's maznun is known qat'an, and fiqh is qat'i knowledge; as for zann, it is a means to it. His statement: 'And that 'ilm is literal in what is not tasawwur also' is a second answer to the previous objection: 'Defining fiqh with 'ilm is not correct.' The summary of the answer: 'ilm does not only mean yaqin and i'tiqad jazim; rather 'ilm is applied to two meanings: one on yaqin and i'tiqad jazim, and the second on non-tasawwur, and the second meaning is general covering both i'tiqad jazim and zann. Therefore in the definition of fiqh, the 'ilm mentioned intends this general meaning so that both yqini and zanni are included, and it does not necessitate that fiqh is only qat'i or that zanniyat are excluded from fiqh.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute defending the characterization of fiqh as 'ilm (knowledge). The objection is that fiqh is primarily based on zanni (speculative) evidence, while 'ilm conventionally means certain belief. The author gives two responses. First: The rulings that a mujtahid derives from zanni evidence become certain for him in practice because he must act upon them definitively due to a qat'i proof (ijma) that his ijtihad is authoritative. The quote from Sharh Minhaj provides a logical syllogism: the mujtahid's zanni ruling must be acted upon qat'an; any ruling that must be acted upon qat'an is known qat'an to be Allah's ruling; therefore the zanni ruling is known qat'an. Hence fiqh is qat'i knowledge, and zann is merely a means. Second: 'Ilm has two meanings: (1) certain belief, and (2) the opposite of tasawwur (mental representation), i.e., any cognitive affirmation. The second meaning includes both certain and speculative beliefs. In the definition of fiqh, 'ilm is used in this general sense to cover both qat'i and zanni rulings. Thus the objection is refuted.

Key Terms
اجماع آحادی (ijma aahadi): Consensus transmitted by a few (aahaad) as opposed to tawaatur.
ادلہ ظنیہ (adillah zanniyyah): Evidences that yield speculative (zanni) knowledge, such as khabar wahid and qiyas.
علم یقینی قطعی (ilm yaqini qat'i): Knowledge that is certain and definitive, leaving no room for doubt.
مجتہد (mujtahid): A scholar qualified to derive rulings from the primary sources through ijtihad.
ظن (zann): Speculation or probabilistic belief, the predominant opinion without certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the mujtahid's zanni ruling considered certain (qat'i) in the Hanafi view?
A) Because the zanni evidence directly gives certainty.
B) Because qat'i ijma establishes that the mujtahid's knowledge is certain.
C) Because zann is the same as yaqin.
D) Because the ruling is from the Quran or mutawatir sunnah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defends the certainty of fiqh through both the qat'i nature of ijma and the broader definition of 'ilm, ensuring that fiqh remains 'ilm despite speculative elements.

The Definition of Fiqh: Why Restricting to Qat'i Rulings Fails
Presenting and critiquing the definition of fiqh by some scholars as knowledge of qat'i rulings with istinbat ability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three objections to the well-known definition of fiqh and evaluate the adequacy of Sadr al-Shari'ah's restricted definition.

Core Idea
Defining fiqh as knowledge of qat'i rulings is too narrow — it excludes the zanni majority of fiqh.

In Hanafi usul, the definition of fiqh is itself a subject of debate. Some scholars, like Sadr al-Shari'ah, attempted to refine the definition to avoid certain philosophical objections. However, as the text shows, this refinement introduces new problems. In this lesson, we examine the critique of the restricted definition and understand why the well-known definition prevails.

Guided Path
1
Identify the proposed definition
Understand the definition of fiqh as knowledge of qat'i rulings with istinbat ability.
This is the definition attributed to Sadr al-Shari'ah in al-Tawdih.
2
Understand the reasoning behind it
Sadr al-Shari'ah proposed this to avoid three objections: excluding classical fuqaha, including muqallids, and using 'ilm for zanni matters.
The objections are detailed in the commentary.
3
Identify the critique
The author of Muslim al-Thubut points out that this definition excludes rulings based on zanni evidences, which are numerous.
Example: most hadith are ahad, giving zanni knowledge.
4
Evaluate the critique
Consider whether the critique is valid: the definition fails to cover the majority of fiqh issues.
The author calls adhering to this definition 'without necessity'.
5
Contrast with the well-known definition
The accepted Hanafi definition includes both qat'i and zanni rulings, and requires istinbat ability for the jurist, not the definition itself.
The well-known definition: knowledge of practical legal rulings derived from detailed evidences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متن المسلم : " وبعضهم جعل الفقه عبارة عن العلم بالاحكام القطعية مع ملكة الاستنباط ويلزم عليه خروج المسائل الثابتة بالادلة الظنية وهي كثيرة الاترى أن السنة المتواترة قليلة جدا والتزام ذالك بلالزوم وجعل العمل داخلا في تحديد هذا العلم كما ذهب اليه بعض مشائخنا بعيد جداً ترجمه : اور بعض اصولیین نے قرار دیا ہے کہ ملکہ استنباط کے ساتھ احکام قطعیہ کے جاننے کا نام فقہ ہے لیکن فقہ کی اس تعریف پر ان مسائل کا فقہ سے خارج ہونا لازم آتا ہے جو ادلہ ظنیہ سے ثابت ہیں حالانکہ ان کی تعداد بہت ہے کیا تم نہیں دیکھتے ہو کہ سنت متواترہ کی تعداد بہت کم ہے اور اس کا التزام بلا ضرورت ہے اور علم فقہ کی تعریف میں عمل کو داخل کر دینا بھی حق سے بہت دور ہے جیسا کہ اس طرف ہمارے بعض مشائخ گئے ہیں۔ تشريح - قوله وبعضهم جعل الفقه........... بلالزوم درج بالا عبارت میں مصنف نے صاحب توضیح صدر الشریعہ کی ذکر کردہ تعریف فقہ کو بعضه ذکر کر کے ان پر الزام وارد کیا ہے اور اپنے قول ھم سے اشارہ کیا ہے کہ اس تحدید میں صدر الشریعہ تنہا ہیں۔ صاحب توضیح صدر الشریعہ نے فقہ کی تعریف ان الفاظ میں کی ہے۔ الفقه عبارة عن العلم بالاحكام القطعية التى ظهر نزول الوحي با وانعقد الاجماع عليها مع ملكة الاستنباط یعنی فقہ ملکہ استنباط کے ساتھ ان احکام قطعیہ کے جاننے کا نام ہے جن پر نزول وحی کا ظہور ہو چکا ہو اور ان پر اجماع منعقد ہو گیا ہو۔ تعریف مشہور سے عدول کے وجوہ:۔ چونکہ قوم سے منقول تعریف فقہ پر تین زبر دست اعتراضات واقع ہوئے تھے۔ (۱) الاحکام سے اگر جمیع احکام مراد ہیں تو مشہور فقہاء جیسے حضرت امام اعظم و مالک و غیرهما کا طبقات فقہاء سے خروج لازم آئے گا۔ (۲) الاحکام سے اگر بعض احکام مراد ہیں تو مقلدین علماء کا گروہ فقہاء میں داخل ہو جائے گا غرض تعریف جامع و مانع نہیں ہے۔ (۳) فقہ کی تعریف العلم سے کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے کہ علم اعتقاد جازم کو کہتے ہیں جبکہ فقہ کے اکثریات ظنیات پر مبنی ہیں۔ تفصیل گزر چکی ہے۔
Matn of al-Muslim: 'And some made fiqh the expression of knowledge of qat'i rulings with the faculty of istinbat, and it follows from it the exclusion of issues established by zanni evidences, and they are many. Do you not see that the mutawatir sunnah is very few? And adhering to that without necessity and making 'amal included in the definition of this science, as some of our shaykhs have gone to, is very far (from the truth).' Translation: And some usuliyyun decided that the name fiqh is knowledge of qat'i rulings along with the faculty of istinbat, but this definition of fiqh necessitates the exclusion of those issues that are established by zanni evidences, although they are many. Do you not see that the mutawatir sunnah is very few? And adhering to that without necessity, and including 'amal in the definition of this science as some of our shaykhs have gone to, is very far from the truth. Tashrih: His statement 'And some made fiqh... bī lā lūzūm': In the above expression, the author (Muslim al-Thubut) mentions the definition of fiqh mentioned by Sahib al-Tawdih Sadr al-Shari'ah in part, and casts an objection upon him, and by his statement 'hum' indicates that in this definition Sadr al-Shari'ah is alone. Sahib al-Tawdih Sadr al-Shari'ah defined fiqh in these words: 'Fiqh is the expression of knowledge of the qat'i rulings upon which the revelation of the wahi has appeared and upon which ijma has been concluded, along with the faculty of istinbat.' That is, fiqh is the name of knowing those qat'i rulings upon which the revelation of wahi has appeared and upon which ijma has been concluded, along with the faculty of istinbat. Reasons for deviating from the well-known definition: Because three strong objections were raised against the definition of fiqh transmitted from the people (the earlier scholars): (1) If by 'al-ahkam' all rulings are meant, then the well-known fuqaha such as Imam al-A'zam and Malik and others would be excluded from the ranks of fuqaha. (2) If by 'al-ahkam' some rulings are meant, then the group of muqallid scholars would enter among the fuqaha. In short, the definition is not comprehensive and exclusive. (3) Defining fiqh with 'ilm is not correct because 'ilm is called i'tiqad jazim (firm belief), while most of fiqh is based on zanniyat. The detail has passed.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage presents a debate on the definition of fiqh. The matn from Muslim al-Thubut quotes an opinion that restricts fiqh to knowledge of qat'i rulings with the faculty of istinbat (deductive reasoning). The author criticizes this definition because it excludes the many issues established by zanni evidences, since mutawatir sunnah (which gives qat'i knowledge) is rare. He also rejects including 'amal (practice) in the definition, as some Hanafi shaykhs did. The commentary (Tashrih) explains that this definition was given by Sadr al-Shari'ah in al-Tawdih. He defined fiqh as knowledge of qat'i rulings on which revelation has appeared and ijma has been concluded, along with istinbat ability. Sadr al-Shari'ah adopted this restricted definition to avoid three objections to the well-known definition of fiqh: (1) If fiqh includes all ahkam (including those of past prophets), then classical fuqaha like Abu Hanifa and Malik would be excluded because they derived rulings not from their own revealed laws. (2) If it means some ahkam, then muqallids (followers who simply memorize and transmit) would be included, which is undesirable. (3) Using 'ilm (certain knowledge) in the definition is problematic because most fiqh is zanni. Sadr al-Shari'ah's definition uses 'ilm qat'i to avoid this. However, the author of Muslim al-Thubut objects that this definition excludes many valid zanni fiqh issues, which is impractical.

Key Terms
الفقه (al-fiqh): In this passage, fiqh is defined variously: some define it as knowledge of qat'i rulings with istinbat ability; the author rejects this because it excludes zanni issues.
العلم بالاحكام القطعية (al-ilm bil ahkam al-qat'iyyah): Knowledge of definitive rulings that are certain and not open to speculation.
ملكة الاستنباط (malakat al-istinbat): The faculty or ability to derive rulings from the primary sources through ijtihad.
سنة متواترة (sunnah mutawatirah): The Prophetic tradition transmitted by a large number of narrators at every level, yielding certainty.
اجماع (ijma): Consensus of the mujtahidun of the ummah on a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author of Muslim al-Thubut, what is the main problem with defining fiqh as knowledge of qat'i rulings with istinbat ability?
A) It includes muqallids as fuqaha.
B) It excludes rulings established by zanni evidences, which are numerous.
C) It requires the faculty of istinbat, which is not well-defined.
D) It makes fiqh a purely practical science.

Key Takeaway
Fiqh in practice encompasses both qat'i and zanni rulings; any definition that excludes zanni rulings is insufficient.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced
8 min
Sadr al-Sharia's Definition of Fiqh: Qat'i Rulings Only?
Critique and defense of a narrow definition of fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the rationale behind Sadr al-Sharia's definition of fiqh and evaluate the criticism that it excludes most of Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Fiqh cannot be defined solely as knowledge of certain rulings, else most of Hanafi fiqh is excluded.

This passage presents a critical dispute in Hanafi usul al-fiqh over the very definition of fiqh. Sadr al-Sharia proposed a narrow definition to avoid certain logical objections, but the majority of scholars objected that it excludes the predominant part of fiqh—rulings based on probable evidences. Understanding this debate is crucial for grasping the scope and nature of fiqh as a discipline.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three objections to the common definition
Scan the passage for the three objections Sadr al-Sharia sought to avoid: (1) excluding famous imams, (2) including muqallids, (3) using 'ilm for zanni knowledge. Note how each arises from different interpretations of 'rulings' and 'knowledge'.
These objections are listed with numbers in the text.
2
Understand Sadr al-Sharia's solution
Sadr al-Sharia redefines fiqh as knowledge of definitive rulings (qat'iyat) with the faculty of istinbat. This avoids the three objections: great imams knew the definitives, muqallids lack istinbat, and 'ilm applies to certain knowledge.
The definition is: 'knowledge of definitive rulings that have been revealed and upon which consensus has been concluded, together with the faculty of istinbat.'
3
Analyze the author's criticism
The author (Mulla Sahib) argues that restricting fiqh to qat'i rulings excludes the vast majority of fiqh, which is based on zanni evidences like khabar wahid and qiyas. He notes that mutawatir texts are few, making this commitment 'without necessity'.
The term 'zanniyat' includes khabar wahid, qiyas, and ijma' based on zanni evidence.
4
Note the alternative inclusion of 'amal by Bazdawi
The passage mentions that Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi included action ('amal) in the definition, suggesting another dimension of the dispute. This indicates that the definition of fiqh has implications for whether it is purely theoretical or includes practice.
Bazdawi's view is criticized as 'far from the truth' by the author, but it represents a third position.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical consequence: Under Sadr al-Sharia's definition, a scholar who only knows qat'i rulings without istinbat is not a faqih; under the common definition, knowing zanni rulings with istinbat qualifies. Also, most fatwas on daily issues (based on khabar wahid) would not be considered fiqh under Sadr al-Sharia's definition.
This affects who is considered a faqih and what counts as fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : اور بعض اصولیین نے قرار دیا ہے کہ ملکہ استنباط کے ساتھ احکام قطعیہ کے جاننے کا نام فقہ ہے لیکن فقہ کی اس تعریف پر ان مسائل کا فقہ سے خارج ہونا لازم آتا ہے جو ادلہ ظنیہ سے ثابت ہیں حالانکہ ان کی تعداد بہت ہے کیا تم نہیں دیکھتے ہو کہ سنت متواترہ کی تعداد بہت کم ہے اور اس کا التزام بلا ضرورت ہے اور علم فقہ کی تعریف میں عمل کو داخل کر دینا بھی حق سے بہت دور ہے جیسا کہ اس طرف ہمارے بعض مشائخ گئے ہیں۔

(۲) الاحکام سے اگر بعض احکام مراد ہیں تو مقلدین علماء کا گروہ فقہاء میں داخل ہو جائے گا غرض تعریف جامع و مانع نہیں ہے۔
(۳) فقہ کی تعریف العلم سے کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے کہ علم اعتقاد جازم کو کہتے ہیں جبکہ فقہ کے اکثریات ظنیات پر مبنی ہیں۔ تفصیل گزر چکی ہے۔
مندرجہ بالا تینوں ایرادات سے بچنے کے لئے صاحب توضیح نے تعریف مشہور سے عدول کیا چونکہ ان کے نزدیک احکام سے جمیع احکام خواہ قطعیہ ہوں یا ظنیہ مراد ہی نہیں ہیں کہ فقہا، معتبرین کا گروہ فقہاء سے خروج لازم آئے نہ ہی بعض مطلق ہی مراد ہیں کہ مقلدین کا دخول لازم آئے بلکہ احکام سے بعض معین مراد ہے اور وہ جملہ احکام قطعیہ ہیں جن سے صحیح استنباط کے ملکہ کے ساتھ انکو جانیے کا نام فقہ ہے غرض کل مطلق مراد نہیں ہے اس لئے بعض مسائل کا حکم نہ جاننے کے سبب امام اعظم ابوحنیفہ امام و مالک و غیر ہم فقہاء سے خارج نہ ہونگے اور قید ملکہ استنباط کی وجہ سے مقلدین داخل نہ ہوں گے اور جب فقہ ان کے نزدیک قطعیات سے عبارت ہے تو علم کا اطلاق بھی درست ہے ظنیات سے اعتراضات فضول ہے۔
قطعیہ سے مقید کرنے کی وجہ :- صدر الشریعہ نے اپنی تعریف میں احکام کو قطعیہ کی قید سے اس لئے مقید کیا کہ ظن شارع کی طرف سے مذموم ہے اس میں کوئی کمال نہیں ہے ارشاد باری تعالیٰ ہے ان يتبعون الا الظن ۔ اور ارشاد ہے يايها الذين امنوا اجتنبوا كثيرا من الظن ان بعض الظن اشم . على الاقل ظن قابل مدح نہیں ہے اور یہ حق ہے کہ حضرت شارع علیہ السلام اور آپ کے صحابہ سے فقہاء اسلام کی مدح ثابت ہے اس لئے ماننا پڑے گا کہ فقہ قطعیات کا نام ہے۔ مصنف کا الزام:۔ ماتن ملا صاحب کہتے ہیں کہ فقہ کی تعریف کو قطعیہ کی قید سے مقید کر دینے سے گر چه ایرادت ثلثہ مشہورہ سے تفصی ممکن ہے لیکن اس سے ایک بڑی خرابی لازم آتی ہے وہ یہ کہ فقہ کا معتد بہ حصہ جو ظنیات پر مبنی ہے جیسے خبر واحد، قیاس، اور اجماع احادی وغیرہ سب فقہ سے خارج ہو جائیں گے کیونکہ احادیث متواترہ جو مفید قطع و یقین ہیں کی تعداد بہت کم ہے اور فقہ کے اکثر مسائل دلائل خفیہ سے ہی ثابت ہیں اس لئے قطعیہ کی قید سے مقید کر کے ادلہ خلیہ سے ثابت شدہ مسائل کے خروج کا التزام ایسا التزام ہے جس پر کوئی دلیل نہیں ہے۔
قوله وجعل العمل داخلافى تحديد الخ
اس عبارت سے مصنف نے حنفیہ کے جلیل القدر امام حضرت فخر الاسلام بزدوی پرد کیا ہے
فخر الاسلام نے اپنی معرکۃ الآراء کتاب اصول بزدوی میں کہا ہے کہ فقہ محض علم کا نام نہیں ہے بلکہ علم و عمل
Translation: And some usulis have decided that fiqh is knowledge of definitive rulings together with the faculty of istinbat. But this definition necessarily excludes those issues established by zanni evidences, even though they are numerous. Do you not see that the number of mutawatir Sunnah is very small? And adhering to this is without necessity. Also, including action in the definition of fiqh is far from the truth, as some of our mashayikh have gone to that. Commentary - His statement: 'And some made fiqh...' with inevitability: In the above passage, the author mentions the definition of fiqh mentioned by Sahib al-Tawdih Sadr al-Sharia, partially, and raises an objection against him, and his statement 'some' indicates that in this restriction Sadr al-Sharia is alone. Sahib al-Tawdih Sadr al-Sharia defined fiqh in these words: 'Fiqh is the knowledge of definitive rulings that have been revealed and upon which consensus has been concluded, together with the faculty of istinbat.' i.e., fiqh is knowledge of those definitive rulings whose revelation has become apparent and upon which consensus has been concluded, together with the faculty of istinbat. Reasons for deviation from the famous definition: Because the transmitted definition of fiqh was subject to three strong objections: (1) If 'rulings' means all rulings, then famous fuqaha like Imam al-Azam, Malik, and others would be excluded from the ranks of fuqaha. (2) If 'rulings' means some rulings, then the group of muqallid scholars would enter into the fuqaha. In short, the definition is not comprehensive and exclusive. (3) Defining fiqh with 'knowledge' is not correct because knowledge is certain belief, while most issues of fiqh are based on zann. Details have passed. To avoid these three objections, Sahib al-Tawdih deviated from the famous definition because in his view, 'rulings' does not mean all rulings, whether definitive or zanni, so that the group of respected fuqaha would be excluded, nor does it mean some absolute rulings, so that muqallids would enter. Rather, it means specific rulings, and they are all definitive rulings that, when known with the faculty of correct istinbat, are called fiqh. In short, absolute totality is not meant, so Imam Abu Hanifa, Imam Malik, and others will not be excluded from the fuqaha because of not knowing the ruling of some issues. And due to the condition of the faculty of istinbat, muqallids will not enter. And since fiqh in his view consists of definitives, the application of 'knowledge' is also correct; objections from zanniyat are futile. Reason for restricting with 'definitive': Sadr al-Sharia restricted rulings with the condition of definitiveness because zann is blameworthy from the Shari'a—there is no perfection in it. The command of Allah Almighty is: 'They follow nothing but assumption.' And the command: 'O you who have believed, avoid much assumption; indeed, some assumption is sin.' At least, assumption is not praiseworthy. And it is true that praise of the fuqaha of Islam is established from the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his Companions, so it must be accepted that fiqh is a name for definitives. The author's objection: The author (Mulla Sahib) says: While restricting the definition with the condition of definitiveness may resolve the three famous objections, a great flaw necessarily follows: the significant portion of fiqh based on zanniyat, such as khabar wahid, qiyas, and ijma' ahmadi (?) etc., will all be excluded from fiqh. Because the number of mutawatir hadith that yield certainty is very small, and most issues of fiqh are established by subtle evidences. Therefore, restricting with the condition of definitiveness and committing to the exclusion of issues established by subtle evidences is a commitment that has no proof. His statement: 'And making action included in the definition...' With this phrase, the author criticizes the great Hanafi imam Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi. Fakhr al-Islam said in his celebrated book Usul al-Bazdawi that fiqh is not merely the name of knowledge, but knowledge and action.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage discusses a dispute about the definition of fiqh in Hanafi usul. The author begins by stating that some usulis (referring to Sadr al-Sharia) define fiqh as knowledge of definitive rulings together with the faculty of istinbat. The main criticism is that this definition excludes the vast majority of fiqh rulings that are based on zanni (probable) evidences, such as khabar wahid, qiyas, and certain types of ijma'. The author points out that mutawatir reports are few, so most fiqh issues would fall outside the definition. The passage then explains why Sadr al-Sharia proposed this definition: to avoid three objections to the common definition. Those objections are: (1) if 'rulings' is taken generically, famous imams like Abu Hanifa and Malik would not be considered fuqaha because they did not know all rulings; (2) if 'rulings' is taken specifically, muqallids (followers) would be included even without istinbat; (3) defining fiqh as 'knowledge' (ilm) is problematic because knowledge implies certainty, but most fiqh is zanni. Sadr al-Sharia's solution is to restrict fiqh to definitive rulings, thus avoiding the first two objections: the great imams knew the definitive rulings, so they remain fuqaha; and muqallids are excluded because they lack the faculty of istinbat. The third objection is also avoided because definitive rulings are known with certainty, so 'ilm' applies. The author then rebuts Sadr al-Sharia by noting that this restriction excludes too much, implying that the common definition is more acceptable. Finally, the author mentions that Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi included action ('amal) in the definition of fiqh, suggesting another dimension of the dispute. The passage is a typical usul dispute over the proper definition of a fundamental term, with each position having its own rationale and consequences.

Key Terms
ملکة الاستنباط (malakat al-istinbat): The faculty or ability to derive rulings from evidences through ijtihad.
قطعيات (qatiyat): Rulings that are known with certainty from definitive evidences like mutawatir texts and ijma'.
ظنيات (zanniyat): Rulings based on probable evidences such as khabar wahid and qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Sadr al-Sharia restrict his definition of fiqh to qat'i rulings?
A) Because zanni is blameworthy in the Shari'a and implies no perfection.
B) To exclude muqallids from being considered fuqaha.
C) To resolve the three objections to the common definition.
D) To include all rulings regardless of evidence strength.

Key Takeaway
The debate over the definition of fiqh reflects the balance between certainty and comprehensiveness; the Hanafi school ultimately includes zanni evidences, acknowledging the majority of its rulings are probable.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Does Fiqh Cover Only Certain (Qat'i) Rulings?
Definition and objection in usul al-fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key components of Sadr al-Shari'ah's definition of fiqh and evaluate the objection raised by Mulla Sahib.

Core Idea
Sadr al-Shari'ah restricts fiqh to qat'i rulings; Mulla Sahib objects that this excludes most of fiqh.

Sadr al-Shari'ah, in his work al-Tawdih, proposed a definition of fiqh that avoids certain objections by narrowing it to certain (qat'i) rulings. However, this raises a new problem: does it exclude the bulk of Hanafi fiqh, which relies on probable evidence like khabar wahid and qiyas? In this lesson, we dissect his definition and the counterargument.

Guided Path
1
Identify Sadr al-Shari'ah's definition and its motivation
State that fiqh is knowledge of qat'i rulings obtained through the faculty of correct istinbat. Note that he deviated from the famous definition to avoid three objections: that mujtahids would be excluded if they don't know all rulings, and muqallids would be included.
The three objections are from the classic definition of fiqh as knowledge of all ahkam.
2
Understand the condition of qat'iyya and its scriptural proof
Sadr al-Shari'ah argues that zann is blameworthy in Shari'ah, citing Quran 10:36 and 49:12. Since fiqh is praiseworthy, it cannot be based on zann, therefore it must be qat'i.
The verses condemn following zann; hence perfection in knowledge requires certainty.
3
Analyze Mulla Sahib's objection
The matn author argues that this definition excludes the substantial part of fiqh derived from zanni evidences (khabar wahid, qiyas, non-mutawatir ijma). Only a few mutawatir hadith yield certainty.
This is a practical objection: most fiqh rulings are based on probable proofs.
4
Evaluate the dispute
Consider whether fiqh should be defined narrowly (only certain rulings) or broadly (including probable rulings). The Hanafi school generally accepts zanni rulings as part of fiqh, but the debate here is about the ideal definition.
The dispute is methodological: what constitutes 'knowledge' in legal theory?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مندرجہ بالا تینوں ایرادات سے بچنے کے لئے صاحب توضیح نے تعریف مشہور سے عدول کیا چونکہ ان کے نزدیک احکام سے جمیع احکام خواہ قطعیہ ہوں یا ظنیہ مراد ہی نہیں ہیں کہ فقہا، معتبرین کا گروہ فقہاء سے خروج لازم آئے نہ ہی بعض مطلق ہی مراد ہیں کہ مقلدین کا دخول لازم آئے بلکہ احکام سے بعض معین مراد ہے اور وہ جملہ احکام قطعیہ ہیں جن سے صحیح استنباط کے ملکہ کے ساتھ انکو جانیے کا نام فقہ ہے غرض کل مطلق مراد نہیں ہے اس لئے بعض مسائل کا حکم نہ جاننے کے سبب امام اعظم ابوحنیفہ امام و مالک و غیر ہم فقہاء سے خارج نہ ہونگے اور قید ملکہ استنباط کی وجہ سے مقلدین داخل نہ ہوں گے اور جب فقہ ان کے نزدیک قطعیات سے عبارت ہے تو علم کا اطلاق بھی درست ہے ظنیات سے اعتراضات فضول ہے۔
قطعیہ سے مقید کرنے کی وجہ :- صدر الشریعہ نے اپنی تعریف میں احکام کو قطعیہ کی قید سے اس لئے مقید کیا کہ ظن شارع کی طرف سے مذموم ہے اس میں کوئی کمال نہیں ہے ارشاد باری تعالیٰ ہے ان يتبعون الا الظن ۔ اور ارشاد ہے يايها الذين امنوا اجتنبوا كثيرا من الظن ان بعض الظن اشم . على الاقل ظن قابل مدح نہیں ہے اور یہ حق ہے کہ حضرت شارع علیہ السلام اور آپ کے صحابہ سے فقہاء اسلام کی مدح ثابت ہے اس لئے ماننا پڑے گا کہ فقہ قطعیات کا نام ہے۔ مصنف کا الزام:۔ ماتن ملا صاحب کہتے ہیں کہ فقہ کی تعریف کو قطعیہ کی قید سے مقید کر دینے سے گر چه ایرادت ثلثہ مشہورہ سے تفصی ممکن ہے لیکن اس سے ایک بڑی خرابی لازم آتی ہے وہ یہ کہ فقہ کا معتد بہ حصہ جو ظنیات پر مبنی ہے جیسے خبر واحد، قیاس، اور اجماع احادی وغیرہ سب فقہ سے خارج ہو جائیں گے کیونکہ احادیث متواترہ جو مفید قطع و یقین ہیں کی تعداد بہت کم ہے اور فقہ کے اکثر مسائل دلائل خفیہ سے ہی ثابت ہیں اس لئے قطعیہ کی قید سے مقید کر کے ادلہ خلیہ سے ثابت شدہ مسائل کے خروج کا التزام ایسا التزام ہے جس پر کوئی دلیل نہیں ہے۔
In order to avoid the three aforementioned objections, the author of al-Tawdih deviated from the famous definition. Since in his view, 'ahkam' does not mean all rulings, whether qat'i or zanni, such that the group of mujtahid fuqaha would be excluded; nor does it mean some absolute rulings such that the muqallids would be included. Rather, by 'ahkam' he means specific rulings, and they are all qat'i rulings, knowledge of which with the faculty of correct istinbat is called fiqh. In short, the absolute is not intended, so Imam Abu Hanifa, Imam Malik, and others are not excluded due to not knowing the ruling of some issues. And due to the condition of the faculty of istinbat, muqallids are not included. Since fiqh in his view consists of qat'iyyat, the application of 'ilm is also correct. Objections regarding zanniyyat are futile. The reason for restricting with qat'iyya: Sadr al-Shari'ah restricted ahkam with the condition of qat'iyya in his definition because zann from the Shari'ah's side is blameworthy; there is no perfection in it. The command of Allah Most High: 'They follow nothing but zann', and the command: 'O you who believe, avoid much of suspicion; indeed some suspicion is sin.' At least, zann is not praiseworthy. And it is true that praise of the fuqaha of Islam from the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his companions is established, so it must be accepted that fiqh is the name for qat'iyyat. The matn author's objection: The matn author, Mulla Sahib, says: Restricting the definition of fiqh with the condition of qat'iyya allows escape from the three famous objections, but it leads to a big problem: that the considerable part of fiqh based on zanniyyat such as khabar wahid, qiyas, and ijma' ahad etc. would all be excluded from fiqh, because the number of mutawatir ahadith which give certainty is very small, and most fiqh issues are established by hidden proofs. Therefore, restricting with qat'iyya obligates the exclusion of issues established by hidden proofs—such an obligation is one for which there is no evidence.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a discussion on the definition of fiqh. Sadr al-Shari'ah, in his work al-Tawdih, redefined fiqh narrowly as knowledge of certain (qat'i) rulings, to avoid three objections: that the famous definition would exclude some mujtahids (e.g., if they didn't know all rulings) or include muqallids. He argued that only qat'i rulings constitute fiqh because zann (conjecture) is blameworthy in Shari'ah, citing Quranic verses. However, the matn author (Mulla Sahib) objects that this excludes most of fiqh, which is based on zanni evidence like khabar wahid, qiyas, and non-mutawatir ijma. He considers this a major flaw with no justification. The commentary follows the author's order: first explaining Sadr al-Shari'ah's position, then the objection.

Key Terms
قطعية (qat'iyya): Rulings with certain proof, such as from mutawatir or definitive texts.
ظنية (zanniyya): Rulings based on probable evidence like khabar wahid or qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main objection of the matn author (Mulla Sahib) to Sadr al-Shari'ah's definition of fiqh as qat'iyyat?
A) It excludes mujtahids who don't know all rulings.
B) It includes muqallids.
C) It excludes most of fiqh which is based on zanni evidence.
D) It contradicts the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The definition of fiqh as qat'i rulings only solves some objections but creates a new one: it excludes the majority of Hanafi fiqh based on probable evidence.

Al-Bazdawi's Definition of Fiqh: Knowledge and Action, Critique and Defense
Definition and critique of fiqh including action

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state al-Bazdawi's three-part definition of fiqh, list the objections raised against it, and explain how the later Hanafi scholars defended the definition.

Core Idea
Fiqh is knowledge perfected by understanding and completed by action; objections dissolve when terminology is stipulated.

Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi, a towering Hanafi usuli, defines fiqh not as mere knowledge but as a composite of three elements: knowledge of the law, perfect understanding, and action. This definition provoked sharp objections from the matn author, but later commentators defended it as preponderant. This lesson unpacks al-Bazdawi's definition, the critique, and the resolution.

Guided Path
1
Break down al-Bazdawi's definition
Identify the three divisions: 'ilm al-mashru' (knowledge of the legislated), itqan al-ma'rifah (perfection of understanding through texts and preserving usul with furu), and 'amal (action). Note that fiqh is only complete when all three are present.
Al-Bazdawi divides fiqh into three, not two.
2
Identify the matn author's objections
List the three objections: (1) fiqh is a codified science, so including action mixes categories; (2) a sinful scholar would not be called a faqih, but common usage applies it; (3) fiqh would be composed of two contradictory things (knowledge and action).
The objections target the combination of disparate elements.
3
Examine the Hanafi defense of al-Bazdawi
Study the response from the commentators: (a) fiqh is not a codified science but the knowledge of a mujtahid; (b) the discussion concerns the praiseworthy fiqh praised in revelation; (c) terminology can be stipulated, so there is no contradiction.
The defense shifts the framework from codified science to mujtahid's knowledge and praiseworthy fiqh.
4
Determine the practical consequence
Understand the difference between faqih mutlaq (one who has all three aspects) and faqih min wajh (one who has knowledge but lacks action). The tarjih favors al-Bazdawi's definition.
The thamarah al-khilaf: whether a non-acting scholar is called faqih absolutely.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

فخر الاسلام نے اپنی معرکۃ الآراء کتاب اصول بزدوی میں کہا ہے کہ فقہ محض علم کا نام نہیں ہے بلکہ علم و عمل
کے مجموعہ کا نام ہے فخر الاسلام کے الفاظ یہ ہیں۔
LL
النوع الثاني علم الفروع وهو الفقه وانه على ثلثة اقسام علم المشروع
بنفسه والقسم الثانى اتقان المعرفة به وهو معرفة النصوص بمعانيها وضبط الاصول بفروعها والقسم الثالث هو العمل حتى لا يصير نفس العلم مقصوداً فاذاتمت هذه الاوجه كان فقها فمن حوى هذه الجملة كان فقيها مطلقا والا فهو فقیه من وجه دون وجه
یعنی نوع ثانی علم فروع ہے اور وہ فقہ ہے اس کی تین قسمیں ہیں ( قسم اول) علم مشروع بنفسہ اور قسم دوم انتقان معرفت ہے وہ نصوص شرعیہ کو ان کے معانی کے ساتھ جاننا اور اصول و فروع کو محفوظ کرنا ہے اور قسم ثالث وہ عمل ہے حتی کہ محض علم مقصود نہیں ہے پس جب یہ تینوں صورتیں متحقق ہونگی تو اس کو فقہ کہا جائے گا اور جو ان تینوں اوصاف سے متصف ہوگا وہ فقیہ مطلق کہلائے گا ورنہ من وجہ فقیہ ہو گا اور من وجہ فقیہ نہ ہوگا“
رد مصنف : - حضرت فخر الاسلام کی اس تحقیق انیق پر اعتراض کرتے ہوئے پر مصنف کہتے ہیں کہ ان کی یہ بات حق وصواب سے دور ہے اس لئے کہ فقہ اگرعلم ملک مجموعہ کا نام ہوتو کی خرابیاں لازم آتی ہیں۔ اولاً: فقہ علوم مدونہ میں سے ایک علم ہے جبکہ بقول فخر الاسلام اس کا علم و عمل سے مرکب ہونالازم آتا ہے۔ ثانیاً:۔ عالم جو اپنے علم کے مقتضی پر عمل نہیں کرتا اس کا گروہ فقہاء سے خروج لازم آتا ہے حالانکہ فقیہ فاسق پر فقیہ کا اطلاق شائع وذائع ہے۔
ثالثا : ۔ فقہ کا دو مقولہ متبائنہ سے مرکب ہونالازم آئے گا اور یہ جائز نہیں ۔
ماتن کی پیش کردہ وجوہ بعد یت پر حضرات شارحین اور حاشیہ نگاروں نے منع وارد کئے ہیں اور کہے ہیں کہ فخر الاسلام کی بات راجح ہے اس لئے کہ اصطلاح میں کوئی مناقشہ نہیں ہوتا ۔ فخر الاسلام کی یہ اصطلاح ہے انہوں نے فقہ کوعلم وعمل کا مجموعہ قراردیا ہے، رہے وجوہ بعد یت تو اس کا جواب ترتیب وار یہ ہے۔ (۱) فقہ علوم مدونہ کا نام نہیں ہے بلکہ فقہ علم مجتہد سے عبارت ہے۔
(۲) کلام اس فقہ مطلق کے بارے میں ہے جس کی مدح کلام شارع میں آئی ہے غرض یہ کہ معرف فقہ
His statement: 'And he made 'amal included in the definition...' With this expression the author (of the matn) criticizes the great imam of the Hanafis, Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi. Fakhr al-Islam said in his famous book Usul al-Bazdawi that fiqh is not merely the name for knowledge, but the name for the combination of knowledge and action. The words of Fakhr al-Islam are: The second type is the knowledge of branches, which is fiqh, and it is of three divisions: first, knowledge of what is legislated in itself; second, perfection of knowing it, i.e., knowing the texts with their meanings and preserving the principles with their branches; third, action, so that mere knowledge is not the goal. When these aspects are complete, it is called fiqh. Whoever encompasses this totality is an absolute faqih; otherwise he is a faqih from one aspect and not from another. The author's refutation: Fakhr al-Islam's fine research is far from truth and correctness because if fiqh is the name for a collection of knowledge and action, several problems arise: First, fiqh is one of the codified sciences, but according to Fakhr al-Islam it would be composed of knowledge and action. Second, a scholar who does not act upon his knowledge would be excluded from the fuqaha, whereas the term 'faqih' is commonly applied to a sinful faqih. Third, fiqh would be composed of two contradictory things, which is not permissible. Response: The commentators and glossators have refuted these objections and said that Fakhr al-Islam's view is preponderant because there is no problem in terminology; his terminology defines fiqh as a combination of knowledge and action. As for the objections, they are answered sequentially: (1) Fiqh is not the name of a codified science; rather fiqh is the knowledge of a mujtahid. (2) The discussion concerns absolute fiqh that is praised in the words of the Lawgiver. In short, the definition of fiqh...
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage presents Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi's definition of fiqh as including both knowledge (ilm) and action (amal). He divides fiqh into three parts: knowledge of the law itself, perfect understanding of texts and principles, and actual practice. The matn author (the commentator) objects, arguing that this makes fiqh a composite of two disparate things, excludes the sinful faqih, and turns fiqh into a codified science that includes non-scientific elements. However, later scholars (shuruh and hawashi) defend al-Bazdawi, stating that terminology can be stipulated, and that the definition applies to the praiseworthy absolute fiqh. The commentary explains that fiqh in this context is not a codified science but rather the knowledge possessed by a mujtahid, and the objections are not valid.

Key Terms
فقه (fiqh): In this passage, fiqh is defined by al-Bazdawi as a combination of knowledge and action.
عمل (amal): Action, practice; included in the definition of fiqh by al-Bazdawi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Bazdawi, what are the three divisions of fiqh?
A) Knowledge of usul, knowledge of furu, and action.
B) Knowledge of what is legislated, perfection of knowledge, and action.
C) Knowledge of texts, knowledge of rulings, and knowledge of proofs.
D) Knowledge of Allah, knowledge of Shari'ah, and knowledge of the world.

Key Takeaway
Al-Bazdawi's definition of fiqh as knowledge, understanding, and action was contested but upheld by later Hanafi scholars as the preponderant view.

Resolving the Contradiction: Action in the Definition of Fiqh
Resolving a contradiction in Fakhru al-Islam's statements on whether action is part of fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and resolve the apparent contradiction in Fakhru al-Islam's statements by applying the Hanafi distinction between complete and deficient fiqh.

Core Idea
Fiqh can be perfect (knowledge+action) or deficient (knowledge only); both are valid definitions depending on context.

This passage tackles a crucial usul issue: is action ('amal) a necessary component of fiqh? Fakhru al-Islam's statements appear contradictory, but the Hanafi tradition resolves this by distinguishing between the complete faqih and the mere knower. Understanding this distinction is essential for grasping the scope of fiqh as a science.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting statements
Locate Fakhru al-Islam's initial statement that seems to include action in fiqh and his later statement that seems to exclude it. Note the exact wording from the passage.
The initial statement suggests fiqh is knowledge and action; the later suggests it is only knowledge.
2
Understand the doubt raised by critics
Recognize why some thought Fakhru al-Islam contradicted himself. The doubt is that his initial and final speeches conflict.
This doubt is addressed in the 'Refutation of a doubt' section.
3
Apply Imam al-Bazdawi's classification
Recall that Imam al-Bazdawi divided jurists into two types: the complete faqih (knowledge+action) and the deficient (knowledge only). See how this classification is used in the passage.
Al-Bazdawi's division is the key to the resolution.
4
Map Fakhru al-Islam's statements to the two types
Notice that the initial statement refers to the complete faqih (perfect fiqh) and the later statement refers to the deficient faqih (fiqh as mere knowledge).
Thus, there is no contradiction; he is speaking of two different categories.
5
Conclude the resolution
State that fiqh can be defined either way depending on whether one intends the perfect instantiation or a lesser degree. The definition of a science can include its ideal without excluding imperfect forms.
This preserves the consistency of Fakhru al-Islam's authority.

اشرف النعوت شرح مسلم الثبوت LA ممدوح ہے چنانچہ یہ ظاہر ہے کہ فقیہ بے عمل، فاسق مستحق مدح نہیں ہوتا ارشاد نبوی ہے اذا مدح الفاسق غضب الرب ویهتز له العرش ۔ پس عمل کی قید فقہ کی تعریف میں ضروری ہے لہذا بے عمل فقیہ کا گروہ فقہاء سے خروج جامعیت تعریف کے منافی نہیں ۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ حجاج بن یوسف کو کسی نے بھی فقہاء میں شمار نہیں کیا حالانکہ وہ احکام شرعیہ کو ان کے دلائل سے جاننے والا تھا۔ (۳) ماہیات علوم اعتبار یہ ہیں۔ اور ماہیات اعتبار یہ کا دو مقولہ متبا ئنہ سے مرکب ہونے میں کوئی حرج نہیں۔ محاکمہ :۔ یہاں فیصلہ کن بات یہ ہے کہ امام بزدوی نے فقہاء کو دوقسم میں بانٹا ہے ایک وہ فقیہ جو علم مشروع اور انتقان معرفت سے متصف ہونے کے ساتھ اس کے من مقتضیٰ پر عمل کرنے والا ہے یہ وہ ہے جسکی مدح شریعت میں کی گئی ہے۔ دوسرا وہ جو صرف احکام شرعیہ کا جانکار ہے اور مقتضائے علم پر عمل پیرانہ ہے۔ نوع اول وہ فقیہ مدوح ہے جو اوصاف ثلثہ کا جامع ہے وہی فقیہ مطلق اور فقیہ کامل کہلاتا ہے اور نوع ثانی جو علم تو رکھتا ہے لیکن عمل نہیں کرتا وہ فقیہ کامل نہیں ہو سکتا بلکہ وہ من وجہ فقیہ ہے اور من وجہ اس پر فقیہ کا اطلاق صحیح نہیں کیونکہ اللہ عز شانہ نے علم فقہ وشریعت کو حکمت فرمایا ہے اور حکمت عمل و علم کے مجموعہ کا نام ہے۔ الحاصل فخر الاسلام نے فقیہ فاسق کو مطلقا خارج نہیں مانا ہے بلکہ من وجہ خارج گردانا ہے اور من وجہ داخل مانا ہے چنانچہ فخر الاسلام نے کہا فمن حوى هذه الجملة كان فقيهاً مطلقا (كاملا) والا فهو فقيه من وجه دون وجه لہذا مصنف کا یہ کہنا کہ فخر الاسلام نے علی الاطلاق فقہ میں عمل کو دخل دیا ہے صحیح نہیں ۔ دفع و ہم :۔ ہماری اس تقریر سے وہ ہم بھی دفع ہو گیا جو یہاں کیا جاتاہے کہ فخر الاسلام کا ابتداء کلام آخر کلام کے منافی ہے چونکہ ابتداء کلام سے یہ باور ہوتا ہے کہ فقہ علم و عمل کے مجموعہ کا نام ہے جبکہ آخر کلام سے مفہوم ہوتا ہے کہ فقہ صرف علم کا نام ہے۔ یہ وہم فکر سے خالی ہے بلکہ فاسد ہے کیونکہ فخر الاسلام کا مقصود یہ ہے کہ فقہ دو طرح کی ہوتی ہے فقہ کامل اور وہ ہے جو علم و عمل پر مشتمل ہو ۔ فقہ ناقص اور وہ وہ ہے جو صرف علم پر مشتمل ہو پس ابتداء کلام میں فرد کامل کا ذکر ہے اور آخر کلام میں فرد ناقص کا بیان ہے لہذا ان کے کلام میں تنافی نہیں ہے۔
Praised is [the faqih]. It is apparent that a faqih without action, a transgressor, is not deserving of praise. Prophetic guidance: 'When a transgressor is praised, the Lord becomes angry and the Throne shakes.' Thus, the restriction of action is necessary in the definition of fiqh. Therefore, the exclusion of the group of the actionless faqih from the jurists does not contradict the comprehensiveness of the definition. This is why no one counted Hajjaj ibn Yusuf among the jurists, although he knew the legal rulings from their evidences. (3) The essences of sciences are conventional. And there is no harm in the composition of two mutually exclusive categories for conventional essences. Adjudication: The decisive matter here is that Imam al-Bazdawi divided jurists into two types: one is the faqih who, besides being characterized by legitimate knowledge and mastery of recognition, acts according to its implications; this is the one praised in the Shariah. The second is one who only knows legal rulings and does not act upon the requirements of knowledge. The first type is the praised faqih who encompasses the three attributes; he is called the absolute faqih and the complete faqih. The second type, who possesses knowledge but does not act, cannot be a complete faqih; rather, he is a faqih in one respect and in another respect the application of faqih to him is not correct, because Allah the Exalted has called the knowledge of fiqh and Shariah 'wisdom', and wisdom is the name of the combination of action and knowledge. The conclusion: Fakhru al-Islam did not consider the sinful faqih as absolutely outside [the definition], but rather considered him outside in one respect and inside in another. As Fakhru al-Islam said: 'Whoever possesses this whole is a faqih absolutely (completely), otherwise he is a faqih in one respect but not another.' Hence, the author's statement that Fakhru al-Islam included action in fiqh absolutely is not correct. Refutation of a doubt: By this exposition, the doubt that is raised here is also refuted, that Fakhru al-Islam's initial speech contradicts his final speech, because the initial speech suggests that fiqh is the name of the combination of knowledge and action, while the final speech indicates that fiqh is only the name of knowledge. This doubt is baseless, indeed corrupt, because Fakhru al-Islam's intention is that fiqh is of two types: complete fiqh, which consists of knowledge and action; and deficient fiqh, which consists only of knowledge. So the initial speech mentions the perfect individual, and the final speech mentions the deficient individual. Therefore, there is no contradiction in his words.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is an analysis of the definition of fiqh, specifically whether action ('amal) is a necessary component. The author begins by stating that a faqih who does not act (a sinful faqih) is not praiseworthy, citing a hadith that praising a transgressor angers Allah. Therefore, the restriction of action is essential in the definition. He then references Imam al-Bazdawi's division of jurists into two categories: the complete faqih who combines knowledge and action, and the incomplete faqih who only has knowledge. The passage resolves an apparent contradiction in Fakhru al-Islam's statements: initially he seems to say fiqh includes both knowledge and action, but later he implies it is only knowledge. The resolution is that Fakhru al-Islam referred to two different types: the perfect faqih (complete fiqh) and the deficient faqih (fiqh as mere knowledge). Thus, there is no contradiction. This reflects the Hanafi usul principle that the definition of a science can include its perfect instantiation while allowing for degrees.

Key Terms
فقیہ (faqih): One who knows legal rulings from their evidences
فقیہ مطلق (faqih mutlaq): The absolute faqih who combines knowledge and action, the complete faqih

Key Terms from Source Passage
