The Existence of Hukm Before Revelation: Definitions and Dispute
Analytical discussion of hukm's meaning and dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi definition of hukm as divine address (khitab) to distinguish the substantive dispute from a merely verbal one, and evaluate the Mu'tazila position on rational good and evil.

Core Idea
Hukm before revelation is impossible because divine address requires a Legislator; the dispute with the Mu'tazila hinges on the nature of khitab.

This passage tackles a foundational usul al-fiqh question: does a legal ruling (hukm) exist before the revelation of divine law? The Mu'tazila argued yes, based on their rational ethics. The Hanafi/Maturidi school argued no, grounding hukm in divine address. The text carefully dissects the meanings of 'hukm' to reveal that the disagreement is not merely verbal but concerns the very nature of divine speech and its relation to human actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two meanings of hukm
Recognize that the passage distinguishes between hukm as divine address (khitab) and hukm as the act being the basis for reward/punishment. Also note a third meaning: occupation of liability (ishtighal al-dhimmah).
This distinction is crucial: the Hanafi position uses the first meaning, while the Mu'tazila use the second.
2
Analyse the proposed reconciliation
Some scholars tried to resolve the dispute by defining hukm as the Legislator's consideration (i'tibar), which does not require address. Understand why this answer is rejected by the author.
The criticism is that this contradicts the established definition of hukm among usul scholars.
3
Apply the correct answer (جواب باصواب)
The passage concludes that the real dispute is about the nature of divine address: is it eternal with a temporal relation, or is it entirely temporal? Hanafis say eternal address, temporal relation; Mu'tazila say both are temporal and pre-revelation.
This preserves the substantive nature of the ikhtilaf.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah)
Consider how this dispute affects whether acts are obligated or prohibited before revelation. For Hanafis, no hukm until revelation; for Mu'tazila, reason dictates obligation based on rational good/evil.
This impacts fatwa on pre-revelation actions of those who never received revelation.

Because in this meaning, before the advent of Shari'a, the question of address (khitab) does not arise at all, nor does the affirmation of address without a legislator become necessary, whereas the affirmation of address without an addressed legislator is inconceivable. So the Mu'tazila's statement about hukm has no way. And if by hukm is meant 'the act being the basis of reward and punishment' i.e., the act being the locus of reward and punishment, then on this assumption, despite holding to rational good and evil, that statement would have no meaning that good is rational and hukm is shar'i, nor would the dispute become a verbal one, because those (Mu'tazila) who affirmed hukm before Shari'a took hukm in the second meaning, and those who denied hukm before Shari'a took hukm in the first meaning. Answer: Some great scholars have answered that in the locus of dispute, by hukm is meant the first well-known meaning, not the second, as the objector stated. Rather, here by hukm is meant 'the occupation of the servant's liability with an act' i.e., the servant's liability being occupied with an act. And occupation is that the legislator considers that the servant's liability has a compulsion of an act or a refrain. So when hukm means occupation of the servant's liability, and occupation is the name of the legislator's consideration, then it is possible that hukm exists but address does not, because mere consideration does not need any address or speech... And good and evil do not necessitate the legislator's consideration, as the Mu'tazila hold that they necessitate hukm, because good and evil at most are aptitudes and suitability for receiving reward and punishment. As for whether from the perspective of this aptitude and suitability, the legislator's consideration mentioned relates to occupation of liability with act and refrain, note that the legislator's consideration is not related to that, so there is no hukm. Summary: Even if there is agreement that good and evil are revealed, if hukm is taken to mean occupation of the servant's liability, then the dispute between the parties is valid. Criticism: There is a defect in this answer because the meaning of hukm that the answerer stated contradicts the meaning transmitted from the usuliyyin. So how can the words of the usuliyyin be interpreted with this meaning of hukm? Further, saying that the legislator's consideration does not need any address or speech is prohibited, because internal address and internal speech are precisely that legislator's consideration, and it is eternal, and its relation occurs after Shari'a. The situation of address and consideration is the same, even though they differ in concept. Correct answer: It is that in the locus of dispute, by hukm is meant address (khitab), and there is no doubt that the address of Allah related to the actions of the obligated is eternal, but its relation is created. So it must be that the first, i.e., the address of Allah, is before the advent of Shari'a, and the second, i.e., the relation of address, is after the advent of Shari'a. And the Mu'tazila say that the address and its relation are both created before Shari'a. This is the real locus of dispute. Therefore, the objector's saying that affirming hukm before Shari'a is not correct for every Mu'tazila sect is prohibited because address before Shari'a does not exist. And on the assumption of the second meaning of hukm (the act being the basis of reward and punishment), its meaning is only that the act has the aptitude and suitability for reward and punishment. Then in that case, hukm becomes exactly good and evil, because the meaning of good and evil of an act is also that the act has aptitude and suitability for reward and punishment, whereas the discussion is about that hukm which is other than good and evil, and that is whether good and evil necessitate hukm or not. The Mu'tazila affirm the first, and the Hanafis and Maturidis have gone to the second.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is an analytical discussion of the dispute between the Mu'tazila and the Hanafi/Maturidi school regarding the existence of hukm (legal ruling) before the advent of revelation (qabl wurud al-shar'). The text begins by presenting the argument that if hukm is defined as divine address (khitab), then it cannot exist before the Legislator, so the Mu'tazila position is untenable. If hukm is defined as the act being the locus of reward and punishment, then the dispute becomes merely verbal: those who affirm pre-revelation hukm take the second meaning, and those who deny take the first. The author then records a response by some eminent scholars ('ulama') who propose that in this dispute, hukm means 'occupation of the servant's liability' (ishtighal al-dhimmah), which is a mere consideration (i'tibar) of the Legislator and does not require actual address. They argue that good and evil (husn wa qubh) do not necessitate the Legislator's consideration, so hukm is not established. The author notes that this answer has defects because it deviates from the usuliyyin's definition of hukm. The correct answer (جواب باصواب) is that in this dispute, hukm means the eternal divine address (al-khitab al-qadim), but its relation (ta'alluq) to human actions is temporal. The Mu'tazila hold both the address and its relation to be temporal and pre-revelation. The Hanafis and Maturidis hold the address eternal but its relation created. Thus the dispute is not verbal but substantive regarding the nature of divine address.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm): In this passage, hukm is analyzed in two senses: (1) divine address (khitab) related to actions of the obligated, (2) the act being the basis for reward and punishment (kawn al-fi'l manatan al-thawab wa al-'iqab). Also defined as occupation of liability (ishtighal al-dhimmah).
خطاب (khitab): Address; specifically the eternal divine speech (kalam nafsi) that relates to human actions.
حسن و قبح (husn wa qubh): Goodness and badness of acts; this passage discusses whether they are rational or revealed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct answer (جواب باصواب) in this passage, what is the nature of divine address (khitab) and its relation to actions?
A) Both the address and its relation are temporal and occur after revelation.
B) The address is eternal, but its relation to actions is temporal.
C) Both the address and its relation are eternal.
D) The address is temporal but its relation is eternal.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position on hukm before revelation rests on defining hukm as divine address (khitab), which is eternal but whose relation to actions is temporal; thus hukm does not exist before revelation.

The Second and Third Categories of Husn and Qubh: Theoretical and Revelation-Based
Classifies actions by how moral value is known: theoretical (nazari) or revelation-based (shar'i).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three categories of husn and qubh (badihi, nazari, shar'i) and classify any given act's moral value according to how it is known, applying the Hanafi principle that reason can independently determine moral value for nazari acts.

Core Idea
Reason alone judges harmful truth as good and beneficial falsehood as evil; only revelation tells us the value of fasting on specific days.

In Hanafi usul, the moral value (husn/qubh) of an act can be known in three ways: self-evident (badihi), through reflection (nazari), or solely through revelation (shar'i). The first category includes acts like justice being good and injustice evil—obvious to anyone. The passage you are about to read explains the second and third categories. You will learn how reflection can reveal the true moral worth of acts that initially appear deceptive, and why some acts—like fasting on a festival day—can only be evaluated by Sharia.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
The passage mentions the second (nazari) and third (shar'i) categories. Recall the first is badihi (self-evident). Note how the text introduces each category with examples.
The first category is not explained in this passage, but it is implied as the opposite of theoretical.
2
Analyze the nazari example
The example is harmful truth (sidq dar) and beneficial falsehood (kadhib nafi'). Understand why reflection shows the former is good despite harm, and the latter evil despite benefit. The text says that after scrutiny, harmful truth is good and beneficial falsehood is evil.
The immediate appearance (harm/benefit) does not determine moral value; deep reflection does.
3
Analyze the shar'i example
The example is fasting on the last day of Ramadan (good) vs. the first day of Shawwal (evil). Note that reason alone cannot decide the value of fasting on these specific days; revelation is required.
Fasting in itself is good every day, but the specific days get their ruling from Sharia.
4
Contrast the two categories
Compare how the moral value is known in each: through reason (nazar) vs. through revelation (shar'). For nazari, reason can independently reach a conclusion; for shar'i, reason has no input and must follow revelation.
This distinction has implications for ijtihad and the use of istihsan.
5
Apply the classification
Given a new act, decide which category it falls into based on whether reason can determine its moral value independent of revelation. If reason can reach a conclusion after reflection, it is nazari; if revelation is needed, it is shar'i.
Some acts may have elements of both, but the classification is based on the primary mode of knowledge.

قوله ومنه ماهو نظري كحسن الصدق الضار الخ
حسن و قبح کے تین اقسام میں سے دوسری قسم کا ذکر ہے مطلب یہ ہے کہ بعض وہ فعل ہے جس کا حسن و قبیح درود شرع کی استعانت کے بغیر نظر و فکر سے ہی معلوم ہو سکتا ہے جیسے صدق ضار کا حسن اور کذب نافع کا فتح ، وغیرہ چنانچہ تدقیق و تامل اور غور و خوض کے بعد معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ فی الواقع صدق ضارحسن ہے اور کذب نافع قبیح ہے گرچہ اول نگاہ میں بظاہر اول ضرر عاجل کی وجہ سے قبیح اور ثانی نفع

قوله ومنه مالايدرك الابالشرع كحسن صوم الخ
حسن و قبح کی تیسری اور آخری قسم کا ذکر ہے یعنی بعض وہ فعل ہے جسکا حسن و فتح شریعت ہی سے معلوم ہو سکتا ہے عقل کو اس میں دخل نہیں جیسے آخری رمضان کے روزہ کا حسن اور پہلی شوال کے روزہ کا فتح ، چنانچہ یہ ظاہر اور واضح ہے کہ صوم فی نفسہ ہر روز حسن ہے لیکن ۲۹ ر رمضان کو اس کا مامور بہ
His statement: 'And from it is that which is theoretical, like the goodness of harmful truth, etc.' This mentions the second of the three types of good and evil. The meaning is that some acts are such that their goodness and evil can be known by reflection and thinking without the aid of revelation, like the goodness of harmful truth and the evil of beneficial falsehood, etc. Thus, after scrutiny, reflection, and deep consideration, it becomes apparent that in reality harmful truth is good and beneficial falsehood is evil, even though at first glance, due to immediate harm, the former appears evil and due to immediate benefit, the latter appears good. His statement: 'And from it is that which is not perceived except through revelation, like the goodness of fasting, etc.' This mentions the third and final type of good and evil. That is, some acts are such that their goodness and evil can only be known from revelation; reason has no involvement in them, like the goodness of fasting on the last day of Ramadan and the evil of fasting on the first day of Shawwal. Thus, it is obvious and clear that fasting in itself is good every day, but on [the 29th of Ramadan?] it is commanded... [text incomplete]
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage explains the second and third categories of husn (goodness) and qubh (evil) in Hanafi usul. The first category (self-evident) is not mentioned here, but the second is theoretical (nazarī): acts whose moral value is known through reflection without relying on revelation. The example given is truthful speech that harms (siddiq dar) — it is good, and false speech that benefits (kadhib nāfi‘) — it is evil, despite immediate appearances. The third category is known only through revelation (shar‘ī): reason cannot determine it. The example is fasting on the last day of Ramadan (good) versus the first day of Shawwal (evil). The text notes that fasting in itself is good, but the specific days obtain their ruling from Sharia.

Key Terms
حسن (ḥusn): Goodness or praiseworthiness of an act from a legal/moral perspective.
قبح (qubḥ): Evil or blameworthiness of an act from a legal/moral perspective.
نظري (naẓarī): Known by reflection and reasoning, not self-evident or purely revealed.
شرعي (shar‘ī): Known only from revelation (Sharia), not by reason.
صدق ضار (ṣidq ḍārr): Truthful speech that causes harm; considered good (ḥasan) after reflection.
كذب نافع (kidhb nāfi‘): False speech that brings benefit; considered evil (qabīḥ) after reflection.
بديهي (badīhī): Self-evident; known immediately without reflection or revelation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which category of husn wa qubh does fasting on the last day of Ramadan belong to?
A) Badihi (self-evident)
B) Nazari (theoretical)
C) Shar‘i (known only by revelation)
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, acts are classified by how their moral value is known: self-evident, theoretical (reason suffices), or revealed (only Sharia decides); knowing this prevents errors in ijtihad.

The Hanafi Doctrine of Kasb: Defining Human Action and Responsibility
Explaining the Hanafi position on human action as kasb and critique of the khalq/kasb distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of kasb, distinguish it from khalq, and apply it to explain moral responsibility.

Core Idea
Kasb: the servant turns God-given power; Allah creates the act. Responsibility arises from this turning.

This passage presents the fourth school—the Hanafi position—on the theological nature of human action. The author first refutes extreme determinism, then engages with the Ash'ari concept of kasb, and finally defines the Hanafi view: the servant does not create but turns the created power (qudra makhluqa) towards a resolve, after which Allah creates the act. This distinction grounds moral responsibility without falling into either compulsion or free-will delegation. We will dissect the definition, the dispute with the Ash'ariyya, and the practical implications for usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the four schools on human action
The passage mentions the Jabri (determinist), Qadari (free-will), Ash'ari (kasb as non-effective), and Hanafi (kasb as effective turning) positions. Locate each in the text.
The Hanafi position is the fourth, presented as the correct one.
2
2. Extract the Hanafi definition of kasb
Find the sentence: 'the turning of the power created by Allah towards the resolve of the act is called kasb.' Note the key components: qudra makhluqa, sarf (turning), 'azm (resolve).
This definition distinguishes Hanafi kasb from Ash'ari kasb.
3
3. Understand the difference between khalq and kasb as per Sadr al-Shari'ah
The passage contrasts khalq (potential occurs in non-locus of power; creator can be alone) with kasb (potential occurs in locus of power; creator cannot be alone). Grasp this attributive distinction.
The author criticizes this distinction as unproductive.
4
4. Analyze the Ash'ari counter-position
Fadil Khayrabadi's presentation: qudra khaliqa vs qudra kasbiyya. The Ash'ari claim that kasb has no efficacy; the servant's power is merely concomitant.
5
5. Apply the Hanafi definition to moral responsibility
The servant's turning (kasb) makes him deserve reward or punishment. Connect this to the concept of taklif (obligation) in usul al-fiqh.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

خیر آبادی:۔ اس جگہ فاضل خیر آبادی نے اشاعرہ کی تقریر کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ جان لو کہ قدرت مؤثرہ کی دوست میں کی جاسکتی ہیں۔ قسم اول : ۔ قدرت کا ارادہ سے ترجیح کے ساتھ متعلق ہونا اس حیثیت سے کہ اس تعلق کے سبب سے ممکن راجح ہو جائے یہی قدرت حقیقیہ ہے جس سے مصنوع صادر ہوتا ہے ممکن موجود ہوتا ہے اسی کو قدرت خالقہ کہتے ہیں جو باری تعالیٰ میں متحقق ہے اور اسی کے ساتھ مختص ہے۔ قسم دوم:۔ قدرت کا ارادہ سے ترجیح کے ساتھ متعلق ہونا اس طور پر کہ ممکن اس تعلق کے سبب راجح نہیں ہوتا بلکہ ارادہ الہی سے متعلق ہونے کے سبب ممکن راج ہوتا ہے۔ اگر چہ قدرت کے اس معنی میں بھی ارادہ ترجیح کے ساتھ متعلق ہے لیکن اس تعلق سے ممکن کا وجود نہیں حاصل ہوتا ہے اسی کو قدرت کا سبہ کہتے ہیں۔ اس طرح تقریر کرنے سے مذہب اشاعرہ بے غبار ہو جاتا ہے کہ اس تقدیر پر نہ تفویض و اعتدال کو راہ ملتی ہے کیونکہ قدرت خالقہ موثر مشکی ہے نہ ہی جبر واضطرار کا واہمہ ہوسکتا ہے اس لئے کہ قدرت کا سبہ دخیل ہے رہے جمادات تو آسمیں مطلقا، ارادہ کو دخل نہیں ہوتا کہ وہ ارادہ سے عاری ہیں۔ قوله عند الحنفية الكسب وصرف القدرة المخلوقة الخ مذہب چہارم: زیر بحث مسئلہ میں چوتھا مذہب حنفیہ کا ہے درج بالا عبارت میں مصنف نے مذہب احناف ہی کو بیان کیا ہے۔ مذہب احناف یہ ہے کہ بندہ کو قدرت کا سبہ حاصل ہے لیکن کسب کا وہ معنی نہیں کہ بندہ کو صرف قدرت و ہمیہ حاصل ہوتی ہے جیسا کہ اشاعرہ کہتے ہیں بلکہ کسب کا معنی یہ ہے کہ بندہ جس فعل کو کرنا چاہتا ہے اس سے پہلے اللہ عز شانہ کی طرف سے بندہ کے اندر اس فعل خاص کی قدرت واستطاعت پیدا ہوتی ہے پھر جب بندہ اسی قدرت مخلوقہ کو فعل خاص کے عزم کی طرف پھیرتا ہے تو باری تعالی فعل کا خلق فرما دیتا ہے پس من جانب اللہ پیدا کردہ قدرت کو عزم فعل کی طرف پھیرنے کا نام کسب ہے جو بندہ کے اختیار میں ہے جس کی وجہ سے بندہ جبر سے نکل کر اختیار کی طرف پہونچتا ہے اس وقت بندہ کو مکلف بنانا اور عقاب و ثواب کا مستحق قرار دینا صحیح ہوتا ہے۔ غرض یہ کہ قدرت فعل اور نفس فعل دونوں کا خالق اللہ تعالیٰ ہے اور اس قدرت مخلوقہ کے صرف واختیار کا مؤثر بندہ ہے چنانچہ بندہ جب جب اس قدرت مخلوقہ کا استعمال کرتا ہے تو اللہ عز شانہ اس فعل کا خلق فرمادیتا ہے گو کہ بعض اعیان واوقات میں جیسے منجزات انبیاء یا کرامات اولیاء کی وجہ سے صرف قدرت کے باوجود فعل کا خلق نہیں ہوتا مگر جب کوئی مانع حسی نہ ہو تو اس عزم کے وقت ضرور فعل کا وجود ہو جاتا ہے۔ اس مقام پر ماتن نے حاشیہ آرائی کرتے ہوئے کہا ہے ۔ "الفرق بين الخلق والكسب على ماقال صدر الشريعة بان الاول امر اضافي يجب ان يقع به المقدور في لامحل القدرة ويصح انفراد القادر بايجاد ذالك المقدور والثانی امراضافي يقع به المقدور فى محل القدرة ولا يصح انفراد القادر بالايجاد فالكسب لا يوجب وجود المقدور لا يعود الى محصل ينتفع به في هذا المقام كمالاً لا يخفى على دقيق المتأمل" یعنی صدر الشریعہ نے توضیح میں خلاق و کسب کے درمیان جو فرق بیان کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ خلق ایک امراضافی ہے جس سے مقدور قدرت کے غیر محل میں واقع ہوتا ہے یعنی اللہ کا فعل مخلوق ایسا مقدور ہے جو خالق کی قدرت کے محل میں نہیں واقع ہوتا اور اس مقدور کے ایجاد سے قادر کا منفرد ہونا صحیح ہے چنانچہ اللہ عز شانہ مستقل بلا کسب عبد مقدور کو پیدا کر سکتا ہے۔ اور کسب ایک امراضافی ہے جس سے مقصد در محل قدرت میں واقع ہوتا ہے لیکن قادر کا اس مقدور کے ایجاد سے الگ ہونا صحیح نہیں ہے چنانچہ عبد کا سب مستقل بغیر تا ثیر قدرت الہیہ مکسوب کو وجود نہیں دے سکتا غرض ، کسب مقدور کے وجود کو لازم نہیں کرتا ، اس طرح خلق و کسب کے درمیان فرق کرنا کسی ایسے ماحصل کی طرف راجع نہیں ہوتا جو اس مقام میں نفع بخش ہو جیسا کہ دوراندیش اور گہری سوچ رکھنے والے پر پوشیدہ نہیں ہے۔ فرق خلق و کسب توضیح کی درج بالا عبارت میں خلق و کسب کے درمیان دوطریقے سے فرق بیان کیا گیا ہے (۱) خلق : الہ تعالی کی ایک ایسی صفت ہے جس سے مقدور مخلوق خلاق کی قدرت کے غیر حل میں واقع ہوتا ہے۔ کسب : بندہ کی ایک ایسی صفت ہے جس سے مقدور و کسب کا سب کی قدرت کے محل میں واقع ہوتا ہے۔
[The passage begins mid-sentence:] there was no involvement of his own choice. In this case, the servant's example is nothing more than that of a saw or a knife, which is undoubtedly completely compelled. For this reason, the author (matn) said: "The truth is that it is sufficient for compulsion." The issue of Fadil Khayrabadi: At this juncture, Fadil Khayrabadi, presenting the Ash'ari position, said: Know that effective power can be divided into two types. First type: Power is related to will with preference, such that by this relation the possible becomes preponderant. This is real power (qudra haqiqiyya), from which the created thing emanates and the possible comes into existence. This is called creative power (qudra khaliqa), which is realized in Allah Most High and is specific to Him. Second type: Power is related to will with preference in such a way that the possible does not become preponderant due to this relation, rather the possible becomes preponderant due to its relation to the divine will. Although in this meaning of power, the will is also related with preference, but the existence of the possible is not obtained from this relation. This is called power of acquisition (qudra kasbiyya). With this presentation, the Ash'ari school becomes clear: on this estimation, neither free will nor moderation gain a path, because creative power is effective; nor can the notion of compulsion and coercion arise, because power of acquisition is intervening. As for inanimate objects, then absolutely no will enters—they are devoid of will. His statement: "According to the Hanafis, acquisition (kasb) is the turning of the created power, etc." The fourth school: On the matter under discussion, the fourth school is that of the Hanafis. In the above passage, the author has explained only the Hanafi madhhab. The Hanafi school is this: The servant possesses power of acquisition (qudra kasbiyya), but kasb does not mean that the servant merely has imaginary power, as the Ash'aris say. Rather, the meaning of kasb is this: Before the servant intends to do an act, Allah—mighty is His glory—creates in the servant power and ability for that specific act. Then, when the servant turns this created power towards the resolve of the specific act, Allah—most high—creates the act. So, the turning of the power created by Allah towards the resolve of the act is called kasb, which is in the servant's control, by which the servant exits from compulsion and arrives at choice. At that time, making the servant obligated and deserving reward and punishment becomes correct. In short, both the power and the act itself are created by Allah, and the servant is the effective agent in the turning and choosing of this created power. Thus, whenever the servant uses this created power, Allah—mighty is His glory—creates the act. However, in some individuals and times—such as miracles of prophets or marvels of saints—the act is not created despite the power, but when there is no sensory obstacle, the act necessarily comes into existence at the time of that resolve. At this point, the author (matn) commented: "The difference between creation (khalq) and acquisition (kasb) according to what Sadr al-Shari'ah said is that the first is an attributive matter by which the potential occurs in a non-locus of power, and it is valid for the powerful one to be alone in bringing about that potential. The second is an attributive matter by which the potential occurs in the locus of power, and it is not valid for the powerful one to be alone in bringing about [the act]. So acquisition does not necessitate the existence of the potential; it does not return to a result that is beneficial in this context, as is not hidden from one of deep reflection." That is, Sadr al-Shari'ah, in al-Tawdih, while explaining the difference between creation and acquisition, said: Creation is an attributive matter through which the potential occurs in a non-locus of power—i.e., the created act of Allah is a potential that does not occur in the locus of the Creator's power—and it is valid for the Powerful to be alone in bringing about this potential. Thus, Allah—mighty is His glory—can independently create the servant's potential without acquisition. Acquisition is an attributive matter through which the potential occurs in the locus of power, but it is not valid for the powerful one to be alone in bringing about this potential. Accordingly, the servant's acquisition cannot independently give existence to the acquired without the effect of divine power. In short, acquisition does not necessitate the existence of the potential. In this way, distinguishing between creation and acquisition does not lead to any result that is beneficial in this context, as is not hidden from the far-sighted and deep-thinking. The difference between creation and acquisition: In the above passage from al-Tawdih, the difference between creation and acquisition is explained in two ways: (1) Creation: an attribute of Allah Almighty through which the created potential occurs in a non-locus of the Creator's power. (2) Acquisition: an attribute of the servant through which the potential of acquisition occurs in the locus of the power of the acquirer.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the fourth school—the Hanafi position—on the theological issue of human action, specifically the concept of kasb (acquisition). The author first sets the context by refuting a purely deterministic (Jabri) view, then presents the Ash'ari position via Fadil Khayrabadi, distinguishing between effective creative power (qudra khaliqa) and acquired power (qudra kasbiyya). The core Hanafi doctrine is then stated: the servant acquires an act by turning the God-given power (qudra makhluqa) towards the resolve, after which God creates the act. This turning is kasb, which belongs to the servant, making him morally responsible. The passage concludes with a critical analysis of the khalq/kasb distinction as given by Sadr al-Shari'ah in al-Tawdih, noting that the distinction is unproductive because it does not truly explain how the servant's action is effective without creating. The Hanafi position avoids both free-will (Qadari) and pure compulsion (Jabri) by affirming that God creates both the power and the act, while the servant's directed choice (kasb) is the basis of responsibility.

Key Terms
الكسب (al-kasb): The servant's turning of the God-given created power (qudra makhluqa) towards the resolve ('azm) to perform a specific act. This turning is a real attribution to the servant and is the basis for moral responsibility.
الخلق (al-khalq): An attribute of Allah by which the potential (maqdūr) occurs in a non-locus of power (lā maḥall al-qudra), i.e., an act that comes into existence independently and does not depend on a created power.
القدرة المخلوقة (al-qudra al-makhluqa): The power that Allah creates in the servant immediately before the act. It is an accident that enables the servant to intend and move.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi doctrine of kasb as presented in this passage, what exactly does the servant contribute to his action?
A) The servant creates the act out of nothing.
B) The servant turns the God-given power (qudra makhluqa) towards the resolve to act.
C) The servant simply becomes aware of the act that God compels him to do.
D) The servant provides the material for the act while God provides the form.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi doctrine of kasb affirms that the servant's turning of God-given power is the real basis of moral responsibility, avoiding both compulsion and free-will.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced
12 min
Dispute on Whether Hukm is Aqli or Shar'i: Mu'tazila's First Argument
Usul dispute: Mu'tazila's first rational argument against shar'i hukm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three schools' positions on the nature of hukm and husn/qubh, and evaluate the Mu'tazila's infinite regress argument and its responses.

Core Idea
Hanafi via media: moral good/evil rational, legal obligation revealed.

How do we know that an act is obligatory or prohibited? Is it through reason alone, or only through revelation? The Mu'tazila, Ash'ariyya, and Hanafiyya each offer distinct answers. This lesson unpacks the Mu'tazila's first argument that hukm must be rational, and the Hanafi/Ash'ari response that preserves the necessity of revelation for legal obligation while acknowledging rational moral knowledge.

Guided Path
1
State the three positions
Identify the Mu'tazila, Ash'ari, and Hanafi views on whether hukm and husn/qubh are rational (aqli) or revealed (shar'i).
Refer to the preamble in the commentary.
2
Understand the Mu'tazila's first argument
Read the Mu'tazila's claim: if hukm were shar'i, an infinite regress would arise when a prophet commands looking at a miracle, because the disbeliever could say: 'I will not look until it is obligatory, and it will not be obligatory until I look.' This would silence the messenger.
This is a rational (aqli) proof against shar'i hukm.
3
Analyze the Ash'ari/Hanafi response
The Ash'ari response (which the Hanafiyya agree with regarding hukm) is that the obligation to look does not depend on looking; it is established by shari'a itself. The commentator then refines the argument, showing that even if the regress were plausible, the obligation to show miracles is a divine duty, not dependent on human action.
The answer rejects the premise that obligation requires prior reflection.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical consequence: the disagreement affects whether pre-revelation actions carry legal accountability. For the Hanafi, there is no legal obligation before revelation, but moral categories are knowable rationally.
This is a key difference from both Mu'tazila (who hold legal obligation is rational) and Ash'ari (who deny rational moral knowledge).
5
Draw the Hanafi conclusion
The passage confirms the Hanafi via media: husn/qubh are aqli, hukm is shar'i. The Mu'tazila argument is refuted by showing that obligation is not contingent on the obligated person's reflection.
The truth (al-haqq) is that showing miracles is a divine duty, as stated at the end.

اشرف النعوت شرح مسلم الثبوت
نفی قبل بعثت جمیع احکام کے ترک سے نہیں بلکہ بعض ان احکام کے ترک سے قبل بعثت عذاب منفی ہے
جس کی طرف عقل کو راہ نہیں ہے۔ مصنف کہتے ہیں کہ معتزلہ نے آیت کریمہ کی تاویل میں جوکھینچا تانی کی ہے ان کی صحت ان کی عقلی دلیلوں کی صحت پر موقوف ہے اگر ان کے دلائل تام وصیح ہوئے تو یہ تکلفات مذکورہ صحیح ہو سکتے
ہیں اور ان کی دلیلوں کا حال آئندہ تمکو انشاء المولیٰ معلوم ہوگا۔
اہ تقصی : بعض شارحین نے اس مقام پر معتزلہ کے لئے چھٹکارہ کی راہ نکالی ہے چنانچہ کہا ہے کہ بر بنائے مذہب معتزلہ حسن و قبح ذاتی قبل بعثت اگر چہ ثواب وعقاب کے جواز کو ستلزم ہے کہ وہ لوگ حسن و قتح ذاتی کے ساتھ حکم بھی مانتے ہیں۔ تاہم وجود حکم کے باوجود عقاب کا جواز ضروری نہیں ہے کیونکہ صحت تعذیب کے لئے حکم کی حیثیت علت متمہ کی نہیں ہے جیسا کہ حالت اکراہ میں زبان پر کلمہ کفر جاری ہونے کے سبب عقاب نہیں ہوتا حالانکہ حکم تحریم موجود ہے مگر اس کے باوجود مکرہ سے مواخذہ نہیں ہو رہا ہے اسی طرح ایسا ممکن ہے کہ حسن و قبح ذاتی کے تحقق کے ساتھ حکم بھی متحقق ہو اس کے باوجود تعذیب صحیح نہ ہو بلکہ تعذیب کی صحت، باوجود حکم کے ان شرائط و روابط کی منتظر ہو جو بعد تحقق بعثت متحقق ہونے والے ہیں الغرض
اس صورت میں حسن وفتح کا عقلی ہوتا اور حکم کا پایا جانا عقاب کے جواز کو لازم نہیں کرتا۔ لاٹھی مافیہ۔
متن المسلم : - قالو اولاً لو كان الحكم شرعياً لزم افحام الرسل عند امرهم بالنظر في المعجزات فيقول لا انظر مالم يجب ولايجب مالم انظر قالوا ولا يلزم علينا لان وجوب النظر عندنا من القضايا الفطرية القياس وفيه مافيه والجواب انا الانسلم أن الوجوب يتوقف على النظر فانه بالشرع نظر اولم ينظر وليس ذالک من تكليف الغافل فانه يفهم الخطاب، اقول لو قال لا امتثل مالم اعلم وجوب الامتثال اذله أن يمتنع عمالم يعلم لوجوبه ولا اعلم الوجوب مالم امتثل لكان بمحل من المساغ فيلزم الافحام والحق أن اراءة المعجزات واجبة على الله لطفاً بعباده عقلا او عادة وهو متم نوره ولوكره الكافرون
تـرجـمه : معتزلہ نے (حکم کے عقلی ہونے پر) پہلی دلیل ذکر کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ اگر حکم شرعی ہو تو
رسولوں کو ساکت کر دینا لازم آئے گا رسولوں کے معجزات میں نظر کرنے کا حکم دینے کے وقت ۔ چنانچہ مکلف کہہ سکتا ہے ہم معجزہ میں نظر نہیں کریں گے جب تک ہم پر نظر کرنا واجب نہ ہوگا اور واجب نہ ہوگا جب تک نظر نہ کروں گا انہوں نے کہا کہ (انجام رسول ) کا اشکال ہم معتزلیوں پر وارد نہ ہوگا اس لیے کہ نظر فی المعجز ہ ہمارے نزدیک قضایا فطریۃ القیاس میں سے ہے اور اس میں وہ ہے جو ہے۔ جواب یہ کہ ہم کو تسلیم نہیں ہے کہ وجوب نظر فی المعجزہ نظر پر موقوف ہے کیونکہ وجوب نظر شریعت سے ثابت ہے مکلف نظر کرے خواہ نہ کرے اور یہ تکلیف غافل کے قبیل سے نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ وہ خطاب کو سمجھ رہا ہے، میں کہونگا کہ اگر مکلف نے ( معجزہ میں نظر کا حکم دیتے وقت بنی سے ) کہا کہ میں آپکے معجزہ کے دیکھنے کے حکم کو بجانہیں لاؤ نگا جب تک وجوب امتثال کو جان نہیں لونگا اس لئے کہ مکلف کو اس حکم کی بجا آوری سے رکنا جائز ہے جس حکم کے وجوب کا اس کو علم نہ ہو اور مجھے کو وجوب امتثال کا علم نہ ہو گا جب تک میں آپ کے معجزہ دیکھنے کے حکم کو بجا نہ لائیں۔ تو البتہ دلیل کی یہ تقریر جواز کا محل ہوسکتا ہے پس اسوقت رسول کا افحام و اسکات لازم آئیگا اور حق یہ ہیکہ معجزات کا دکھانا بندوں کو لطف وکرم کے سبب اللہ عزشانہ پر عقلاً یا عادۃ واجب ہے وہ باری تعالیٰ شانہ اپنے نور کو تام فرمانے والا ہے گرچہ کا فرنہ چاہیں ۔ تشریح :- (تمہید ) یا در ہے کہ معتزلہ اور اشاعرہ کے درمیان جسطرح حسن و قبح کے عقلی و شرعی ہونے میں اختلاف ہے ایسے ہی ان کے درمیان حکم کے شرعی و عقلی ہونے میں بھی اختلاف پایا جاتا ہے۔ معتزلہ فعل کے حسن و فتح کو عقلی کہنے کے ساتھ ساتھ حکم کو بھی عقلی کہتے ہیں۔ اس کے برعکس اشاعرہ حکم کو شرعی کہنے کے ساتھ حسن و قبح کو بھی شرعی کہتے ہیں البتہ حنفیہ کا مذہب بین بین ہے دونوں عقلی ہے نہ دونوں شرعی ہی ہے بلکہ فعل کا حسن و قبح عقلی ہے اور حکم شرعی ہے اشاعرہ کی پانچویں اور آخری دلیل جس طرح حسن و قبح کے عقلی ہونے کو باطل کرنے کے لیے قائم کی گئی تھی یونہی حکم کے عقلی ہونے کے بطلان کے لئے بھی قائم کیا ہے الغرض حکم کے عقلی ہونے کی نفی پر اشاعرہ کی دلیل ما سبق میں دلیل پنجم کے ذیل میں گذر چکی ہے اسلئے مناسب تھا کہ اشاعرہ کی دلیل کے بعد معتزلہ کی دلیل حکم کے عقلی ہونے
میں ذکر کی جائے پس مصنف نے ان کی دلیلوں کے ذکر کرنے کا ارادہ کیا تو کہا قالواولاً الخ
The text begins with a commentary on Ashraf al-Nu'ut. [Then:] 'Negation before the advent of prophethood is not from abandoning all rulings, but from abandoning some rulings; before prophethood, punishment is negated for that which reason has no path.' The author says: 'The Mu'tazila, in their interpretation of the noble verse, have exerted effort; its correctness depends on the correctness of their rational proofs. If their proofs are complete and sound, then these strained interpretations can be correct. Their proofs' status will be known to you later, God willing.' Then: 'Ah, clarification: Some commentators have found a way out for the Mu'tazila in this place, saying that according to the Mu'tazila's school, essential good and evil before prophethood, although necessitating the possibility of reward and punishment, and they believe in ruling along with essential good and evil, yet the possibility of punishment is not necessary despite the existence of rule, because for the validity of punishment, the rule is not like an efficient cause. Just as in a state of compulsion, uttering a word of disbelief on the tongue does not cause punishment, although the prohibitory ruling exists, yet the compelled person is not taken to account. Similarly, it is possible that with the realization of essential good and evil, the ruling is also realized, yet punishment is not valid. Rather, the validity of punishment, despite the ruling, awaits those conditions and links that will be realized after the realization of the advent of prophethood.' The text of al-Muslim: 'They said first: If the ruling were shar'i, it would necessitate silencing the messengers when they command reflection on miracles, because he can say: I will not reflect unless it is obligatory, and it is not obligatory unless I reflect.' They said: 'This does not apply to us, because the obligation of reflection is for us among the a priori premises of analogy, and there is what there is in it.' The answer: We do not accept that the obligation depends on reflection, because it is by the shari'a, whether he reflects or not. This is not from the obligation of the heedless, because he understands the address. I say: If he said, 'I will not comply until I know the obligation to comply, because he can desist from what he does not know to be obligatory, and I do not know the obligation until I comply' — then this presentation would be plausible, and thus silencing would be necessitated. The truth is that showing miracles is obligatory upon God as a kindness to His servants, by reason or custom, and He is the One who perfects His light even if the disbelievers hate it.' Translation: The Mu'tazila presented their first argument (for the rationality of ruling) saying: If ruling were shar'i, it would necessitate silencing the messengers when they command looking at miracles. For the obligated person can say: We will not look until looking is obligatory on us, and it will not be obligatory until we look. They said: This problem does not apply to us, because looking at miracles is for us among the a priori premises of analogy, and there is what there is in it. The answer: We do not accept that the obligation of looking depends on looking, because the obligation of looking is established by shari'a, whether the obligated person looks or not. This is not a type of obligation of the heedless because he understands the address. I would say: If the obligated person said (when the prophet commands looking), 'I will not carry out your command to see the miracle until I know the obligation of compliance, because the obligated person is allowed to refrain from a command whose obligation he does not know, and I will not know the obligation of compliance until I carry out your command to see the miracle' — then this presentation of the proof can be plausible. Then the silencing and confusion of the messenger would be necessary. The truth is that showing miracles is obligatory upon God, due to kindness and grace, by reason or custom, and He, exalted, perfects His light even if the disbelievers dislike it.' Commentary: (Preamble) It is that between the Mu'tazila and the Ash'ariyya, just as there is disagreement on whether good and evil are rational or revealed, similarly there is disagreement on whether the ruling is rational or revealed. The Mu'tazila say that the good and evil of actions are rational, and also say that the ruling is rational. In contrast, the Ash'ariyya say that the ruling is revealed, and also that good and evil are revealed. However, the Hanafiyya's madhhab is between the two: it is not that both are rational nor that both are revealed, but rather the good and evil of actions are rational, and the ruling is revealed. The Ash'ariyya's fifth and final argument that was used to invalidate the rationality of good and evil is also used to invalidate the rationality of the ruling. In short, the Ash'ariyya's argument for the negation of the rationality of the ruling has already passed in the context of the fifth argument. For this reason, it was appropriate that after the Ash'ariyya's argument, the Mu'tazila's argument for the rationality of the ruling be mentioned. So the author intended to mention their arguments, and said: 'They said first...' etc.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute on whether legal rulings (hukm) are rational (aqli) or revealed (shar'i). The Mu'tazila argue that if rulings were only known through revelation, an infinite regress would occur when a prophet commands a disbeliever to look at a miracle as proof of prophethood: the disbeliever could claim he cannot look until it is obligatory, but obligation comes only through looking. The Mu'tazila claim this problem does not affect them because the obligation to look is a self-evident (fitri) truth. The Ash'ari/Hanafi response rejects that the obligation depends on looking; it is established by shari'a regardless. The commentator also notes a more plausible formulation of the argument that would indeed entail silencing, but then asserts the truth: showing miracles is a divine obligation by reason or custom. The structural commentary (تشريح) clarifies the three schools: Mu'tazila (ruling and good/evil both rational), Ash'ariyya (both revealed), and Hanafiyya (good/evil rational, ruling revealed). This passage thus demonstrates the Hanafi via media.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm): A legal ruling from Allah concerning the acts of the obligated persons.
عقلي (aqli): That which is known by reason independently of revelation.
شرعي (shar'i): That which is established by divine revelation (shari'a).
حسن و قبح (husn wa qubh): The moral categories of good and evil actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazila's first argument, why would a shar'i hukm lead to an infinite regress?
A) Because the messenger cannot prove his miracle without prior knowledge of obligation.
B) Because the obligated person can demand to know the obligation before obeying, leading to a cycle.
C) Because the shari'a is incomplete without reason.
D) Because the messenger must first know the ruling himself.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the moral quality of acts is known by reason, but the legal obligation (hukm) is known only through revelation.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced
8 min
Mu'tazila's Circularity Argument for Rational Hukm and Hanafi Refutation
Presents Mu'tazila's first proof and Hanafi refutation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Mu'tazila's circularity argument against the Shar'i nature of hukm and apply the Hanafi response that distinguishes husn/qubh from hukm.

Core Idea
Hukm is Shar'i, but its proof does not require a prior obligation to look at miracles — the miracle itself suffices.

This lesson examines the first proof of the Mu'tazila for the rational nature of hukm. They argue that if hukm were Shar'i, a vicious circle would arise: the obligation to look at a miracle depends on prophethood, but prophethood depends on looking. The Hanafi school refutes this by clarifying that the obligation to look is established by Shari'ah itself through the manifest miracle, not by a prior rational obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
What is the disagreement between Mu'tazila and Hanafis regarding the nature of hukm? The Mu'tazila hold both husn/qubh and hukm to be rational; Hanafis hold husn/qubh as rational but hukm as Shar'i.
2
State the Mu'tazila's first proof
Summarize their circularity argument: If hukm is Shar'i, then obligation to look at a miracle depends on prophethood, but prophethood is established by looking at the miracle, leading to a vicious circle. Therefore, hukm must be 'aqli.
This argument is known as the 'circle of obligation' (dawr al-wujub).
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
How do Hanafis break the circle? The key is that the obligation to look at the miracle is not dependent on a prior rational obligation; it is directly established by the manifest miracle itself. The miracle provides immediate rational evidence of prophethood, so no prior Shar'i obligation is needed.
The Hanafi position avoids the circle by denying the dependency claimed by Mu'tazila.
4
Locate the epistemological difference
How does the Hanafi view of husn/qubh differ from both Mu'tazila and Ash'ari? Mu'tazila say both husn/qubh and hukm are rational; Ash'ari say both are Shar'i; Hanafis say husn/qubh are rational while hukm is Shar'i.
This middle position is unique to the Hanafi school.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
What practical difference results from this dispute? For Mu'tazila, the obligation to examine miracles is a rational obligation independent of revelation; for Hanafis, it is a Shar'i obligation, but the rational nature of the miracle compels looking.
The difference affects how one understands the basis of religious obligation.

اشرف المعوت شرح مسلم الثبوت
۲۵۴
قوله قالوا اولا لوكان الحكم شرعيا لزم الخ
درج بالا عبارت میں ماتن نے حکم کے عقلی ہونے پر معتزلہ کی پہلی دلیل ذکر کی ہے انکی اس دلیل کو سمجھنے سے پہلے یہ چند جملے ذہن نشین کر لیں۔
یہ معلوم ہے کہ وجوب و حرمت و غیر ما احکام میں سے ہیں اور حکم خطاب الہی کا نام ہے خطاب اللہ کا نزول بشکل وحی نبی پر ہوتا ہے، پھر نبی کی نبوت کا اثبات معجزہ سے ہوتا ہے پس مکلفین کے نزدیک نبی کی نبوت کا ثبوت و اظہار نبی سے صادر شدہ معجزہ میں نظر کرنے سے ہوتا ہے، الغرض وجوب وغیرہ احکام شرعیہ کا ثبوت نبی کی نبوت کے ثبوت پر موقوف ہے کہ احکام بندوں کو نبی کے ہی ذریعہ ملتے ہیں۔ اور بندوں کے نزدیک نبی کی نبوت اس وقت ثابت ہوگی جب بندے نبی کے معجزہ میں نظر کریں گویا نبی کی نبوت کا ثبوت ان کے معجزہ میں نظر کرنے پر موقوف ہے اب معتزلہ کی دلیل سماعت کریں! دلیل اول: کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ اگر حکم شرعی ہو جیسا کہ اشاعرہ وحنفیہ کہتے ہیں یعنی اگر حکم نبی کی نبوت یا شرع سے ثابت ہو تو نبی کا اسکات و افحام لازم آئے گا اور وہ اپنی نبوت و رسالت کے اثبات سے عاجز و درماندہ ہو جائیں گے وہ اس طرح کہ نبی نے جب اپنے دعوئی بنوت کے اثبات میں معجزہ ظاہر فرما کر مکلفین کو حکم دیا کہ میری دلیل نبوت معجزہ کو دیکھو تا کہ تم میرے دعوی کی تصدیق کر سکو اس پر مکلفین کہہ سکتے ہیں کہ ہم آپ کے معجزہ کو نہیں دیکھیں گے کیونکہ ہم پر مجزہ دیکھنا واجب نہیں ہے اور وجوب نظر فی المعجزہ ہمارے بغیر معجزہ کو دیکھے ثابت نہیں ہو گا اس لئے کہ وجوب نظر حکم ہے اور حکم اس شخص کے قول سے ثابت ہوتا ہے جن کے نبوت کی معجزہ سے تائیکہ ہو گئی ہو پس اس کا قول حق اور انکا امر امر وجو بی قطعی ہوتا ہے۔ لیکن معجزہ دیکھنے کا حکم دیتے وقت ابھی چونکہ نبوت ہی ثابت نہیں ہو پائی ہے تو ان کا امر حکم درجہ وجوب میں نہ ہوگا کہ جب معجزہ میں نظر کرنا ہی واجب نہیں ہوا اور منکرین نے معجزہ بھی نہ دیکھا بلکہ دیکھنے سے انکار کر دیا تو نبوت ہی نہ ثابت ہوئی بلکہ نبی عاجز ولا چار ٹھہرے جائیں گے کیونکہ اس صورت میں وجوب نظر فی المعجز و موقوف ہے ثبوت شرع یا ثبوت نبوت پر اور ثبوت شرع و نبوت موقوف ہے نظر فی امنجز معجزہ دیکھنے پر) پر تو وجوب نظر فی المعجز و موقوف ہو گیا نظر فی المعجزہ پر اور چونکہ نظر فی المعجز و موقوف ہے وجوب نظر فی المعجزہ پر۔ تو وجوب نظر فی المعجز و موقوف ہو گیا وجوب نظر فی المعجزہ پر
The prophets would necessarily be silenced at the time of commanding to look at their miracles. Thus the accountable person can say: 'We will not look at the miracle until looking becomes obligatory upon us, and it will not be obligatory until I look.' They said: 'The objection of the prophet's being silenced does not apply to us Mu'tazila because looking at the miracle is, in our view, among the innate propositions of syllogism, and there is in it what there is.' The answer: We do not concede that the obligation to look at the miracle depends on looking, because the obligation to look is established by the Shari'ah, whether the accountable person looks or not, and this obligation is not of the type of [obligation upon] the heedless, because he understands the address. I say: If the accountable person says at the time of commanding to look at the miracle to the prophet: 'I will not carry out your command to see the miracle until I know the obligation of compliance, because it is permissible for the accountable person to refrain from carrying out a command whose obligation he does not know, and I will not know the obligation of compliance until I carry out your command to see the miracle' — then this exposition of the proof can be a place of possibility, so at that time the prophet's being silenced and confounded becomes necessary. But the truth is that showing miracles is, due to kindness and grace, rationally or habitually obligatory upon Allah, may His glory be exalted, towards the servants. He, the Exalted, is the One who perfects His light, even if the disbelievers dislike it. Explanation: (Introduction) Know that just as there is disagreement between the Mu'tazila and Ash'aris regarding whether good and evil are rational or Shar'i, similarly there is disagreement between them regarding whether the ruling is Shar'i or rational. The Mu'tazila, while saying that the goodness and evilness of actions are rational, also say that the ruling is rational. In contrast, the Ash'aris, while saying that the ruling is Shar'i, also say that good and evil are Shar'i. However, the Hanafi school is in between: both are not rational nor both are Shar'i; rather, the goodness and evilness of actions are rational, and the ruling is Shar'i. The fifth and final proof of the Ash'aris, which was established to invalidate the rationality of good and evil, has likewise been established for the invalidity of the rationality of the ruling. In short, the proof of the Ash'aris against the rationality of the ruling has already passed under the fifth proof in the previous discussion. Therefore, it was appropriate that after the proof of the Ash'aris, the proof of the Mu'tazila for the rationality of the ruling be mentioned. So the author intended to mention their proofs and said: 'They said, first...' 

[Explanation:] The text above, the author has mentioned the first proof of the Mu'tazila for the rationality of the ruling. Before understanding this proof, keep these few sentences in mind. It is known that obligation, prohibition, etc. are among the rulings, and a ruling is the name of the divine address. The revelation of the divine address in the form of revelation comes upon the prophet. Then the establishment of the prophet's prophethood is through miracles. So in the view of the accountable, the proof and manifestation of the prophet's prophethood occurs by looking at the miracle issued from the prophet. In short, the establishment of obligations and other Shar'i rulings depends on the establishment of the prophet's prophethood, because the rulings reach the servants only through the prophet. And in the view of the servants, the prophet's prophethood is established when the servants look at the prophet's miracle. That is, the establishment of the prophet's prophethood depends on looking at his miracle. Now hear the proof of the Mu'tazila! The summary of the first proof: If the ruling were Shar'i, as the Ash'aris and Hanafis say — that is, if the ruling is established by the prophet's prophethood or by the Shari'ah — then the prophet's being silenced and confounded would become necessary, and they would be unable to prove their prophethood and messengership. In this way: When the prophet, in proving his claim to prophethood, manifests a miracle and commands the accountable: 'Look at my miracle, the proof of my prophethood, so that you may verify my claim,' the accountable can say: 'We will not look at your miracle because looking at a miracle is not obligatory upon us, and the obligation to look at the miracle is not established without us looking at the miracle, because the obligation to look is a ruling, and a ruling is established by the statement of a person whose prophethood has been supported by a miracle. So his statement is true and his command is a definite obligatory command. But at the time of giving the command to see the miracle, since prophethood has not yet been established, his command would not be in the degree of obligation. So when looking at the miracle is not obligatory, and the deniers have not seen the miracle but rather refused to see it, then prophethood is not established; rather, the prophet becomes helpless and incapacitated. Because in this case, the obligation to look at the miracle depends on the establishment of the Shari'ah or the establishment of prophethood, and the establishment of the Shari'ah and prophethood depends on looking at the miracle. So the obligation to look depends on looking at the miracle, and since looking at the miracle depends on the obligation to look at the miracle, the obligation to look depends on the obligation to look.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage presents a crucial usul al-fiqh dispute regarding the nature of hukm (ruling). The Mu'tazila argue that hukm must be rational ('aqli), not Shar'i, because if it were Shar'i, a vicious circle (dawr) would arise: the obligation to look at a miracle (to verify prophethood) depends on the establishment of prophethood (since only a true prophet's command is binding), but prophethood depends on looking at the miracle. This would render the prophet unable to prove his prophethood. The Hanafi school, as explained in the commentary, takes a middle position: the goodness/evilness of actions (husn/qubh) are rational, but the ruling (hukm) is Shar'i. The Hanafi response rejects the circle by asserting that the obligation to look at the miracle is established by Shari'ah itself, not dependent on prior looking; the command to look is given by the prophet, but its obligation comes from Allah through the prophet's claim supported by the miracle itself. The author here is refining the matn (Muslim al-Thubut) by explaining the Mu'tazila's proof and then implicitly upholding the Hanafi view. The key is that the obligation to look is known by rational necessity ('aqli) according to the Mu'tazila, but for the Hanafis it is Shar'i yet not circular because the Shari'ah is established through the miracle itself without needing prior obligation. The text also clarifies the distinction between the Mu'tazila, Ash'aris, and Hanafis on this issue.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm): The divine address (khitab Allah) regarding the actions of the accountable, including obligation, prohibition, etc.
حسن و قبح (husn wa qubh): The inherent goodness or evilness of an action, which for Hanafis is rational (not dependent on revelation).
نظر في المعجزة (nazar fi al-mu'jiza): Examining or looking at a miracle to verify a prophet's claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazila's first proof, what would be the consequence if hukm were Shar'i?
A) Prophets would be unable to prove their prophethood due to a vicious circle.
B) All rulings would be known through reason alone.
C) There would be no need for miracles.
D) The Hanafi school would be refuted.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school resolves the Mu'tazila's circularity argument by holding that the obligation to follow a prophet is established by the manifest miracle itself, not by a prior rational obligation, thus affirming that hukm is Shar'i while husn/qubh are rational.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
12 min
Mu'tazila's Circularity Argument and the Hanafi Response
Usul dispute: circularity argument and response

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Mu'tazila's circularity argument against shar'i rulings and evaluate the Hanafi/Ash'arite response using the concept of fitri al-qiyas.

Core Idea
If hukm were solely shar'i, establishing prophethood would lead to a vicious circle; Hanafis break it by affirming rational self-evident obligations.

This passage delves into a foundational usul al-fiqh dispute: is a ruling (hukm) necessarily derived from divine revelation (shar'i), or can it be known independently by reason (aqli)? The Mu'tazila present a clever circularity argument claiming that if hukm is shar'i, then the very process of verifying a prophet's claim becomes impossible. The Hanafis, aligning with the Ash'arites, counter that a key obligation—to examine a prophet's miracle—is a rational necessity that does not depend on prior revelation, thus avoiding the circle. Understanding this debate is crucial for grasping the epistemological basis of Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Unpack the Mu'tazila's circularity argument
Identify the claimed dependency: to know prophethood one must look at the miracle; but looking is only obligatory if the Prophet's command is authoritative, which requires prophethood. This creates a circle that purportedly leaves the Prophet helpless if hukm is shar'i.
Focus on the logical structure: wujub al-nazar ↔ thubut al-nubuwwa.
2
Analyze the Ash'arite objection
The Ash'arites object that even on the Mu'tazila's own rational view, if the obligation to look is theoretical (nazari) rather than self-evident, the same circularity arises: one must first know the obligation before looking.
The objection targets the Mu'tazila's claim that rational obligations avoid the circle.
3
Examine the Mu'tazila's response: fitri al-qiyas
The Mu'tazila reply that the obligation to look at a miracle is a self-evident rational proposition (badihi, fitri al-qiyas) like 'four is even'—immediately known without prior proof. Thus no circle exists.
This concept of innate analogy is key to their defense.
4
Identify the Hanafi position within the debate
Hanafis (and Ash'arites) maintain that hukm is shar'i, but they agree with the Mu'tazila that the obligation to look at the miracle is a rational necessity. However, they argue that this necessity itself is dependent on the intellect's design by the Creator, not on prior Shari'a.
The Hanafi view integrates reason and revelation without circularity.
5
Assess the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The dispute affects the foundation of obligation: for Mu'tazila, reason alone can obligate; for Hanafis, rational necessity points to the need for revelation to specify the content of obligations.
This underpins differences in how rulings are derived in fiqh.

قوله قالوا اولا لوكان الحكم شرعيا لزم الخ

درج بالا عبارت میں ماتن نے حکم کے عقلی ہونے پر معتزلہ کی پہلی دلیل ذکر کی ہے انکی اس دلیل کو سمجھنے سے پہلے یہ چند جملے ذہن نشین کر لیں۔
یہ معلوم ہے کہ وجوب و حرمت و غیر ما احکام میں سے ہیں اور حکم خطاب الہی کا نام ہے خطاب اللہ کا نزول بشکل وحی نبی پر ہوتا ہے، پھر نبی کی نبوت کا اثبات معجزہ سے ہوتا ہے پس مکلفین کے نزدیک نبی کی نبوت کا ثبوت و اظہار نبی سے صادر شدہ معجزہ میں نظر کرنے سے ہوتا ہے، الغرض وجوب وغیرہ احکام شرعیہ کا ثبوت نبی کی نبوت کے ثبوت پر موقوف ہے کہ احکام بندوں کو نبی کے ہی ذریعہ ملتے ہیں۔ اور بندوں کے نزدیک نبی کی نبوت اس وقت ثابت ہوگی جب بندے نبی کے معجزہ میں نظر کریں گویا نبی کی نبوت کا ثبوت ان کے معجزہ میں نظر کرنے پر موقوف ہے اب معتزلہ کی دلیل سماعت کریں! دلیل اول: کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ اگر حکم شرعی ہو جیسا کہ اشاعرہ وحنفیہ کہتے ہیں یعنی اگر حکم نبی کی نبوت یا شرع سے ثابت ہو تو نبی کا اسکات و افحام لازم آئے گا اور وہ اپنی نبوت و رسالت کے اثبات سے عاجز و درماندہ ہو جائیں گے وہ اس طرح کہ نبی نے جب اپنے دعوئی بنوت کے اثبات میں معجزہ ظاہر فرما کر مکلفین کو حکم دیا کہ میری دلیل نبوت معجزہ کو دیکھو تا کہ تم میرے دعوی کی تصدیق کر سکو اس پر مکلفین کہہ سکتے ہیں کہ ہم آپ کے معجزہ کو نہیں دیکھیں گے کیونکہ ہم پر مجزہ دیکھنا واجب نہیں ہے اور وجوب نظر فی المعجزہ ہمارے بغیر معجزہ کو دیکھے ثابت نہیں ہو گا اس لئے کہ وجوب نظر حکم ہے اور حکم اس شخص کے قول سے ثابت ہوتا ہے جن کے نبوت کی معجزہ سے تائیکہ ہو گئی ہو پس اس کا قول حق اور انکا امر امر وجو بی قطعی ہوتا ہے۔ لیکن معجزہ دیکھنے کا حکم دیتے وقت ابھی چونکہ نبوت ہی ثابت نہیں ہو پائی ہے تو ان کا امر حکم درجہ وجوب میں نہ ہوگا کہ جب معجزہ میں نظر کرنا ہی واجب نہیں ہوا اور منکرین نے معجزہ بھی نہ دیکھا بلکہ دیکھنے سے انکار کر دیا تو نبوت ہی نہ ثابت ہوئی بلکہ نبی عاجز ولا چار ٹھہرے جائیں گے کیونکہ اس صورت میں وجوب نظر فی المعجز و موقوف ہے ثبوت شرع یا ثبوت نبوت پر اور ثبوت شرع و نبوت موقوف ہے نظر فی امنجز معجزہ دیکھنے پر) پر تو وجوب نظر فی المعجز و موقوف ہو گیا نظر فی المعجزہ پر اور چونکہ نظر فی المعجز و موقوف ہے وجوب نظر فی المعجزہ پر۔ تو وجوب نظر فی المعجز و موقوف ہو گیا وجوب نظر فی المعجزہ پر۔ یہ دور ہے جس کے دفعہ کی نبی کو بر تقدیر شرعی کوئی راہ نہیں اس لئے ان کا عاجز ہونا لازم آئے گا۔

قوله - قالوا لاويلزم علينا لان وجوب النظر عندنا الخ معتزلہ کی دلیل مذکور پر اشاعرہ نے ایک معارضہ قائم کیا ہے درج بالا عبارت میں معتزلہ نے اشاعرہ کے معارضہ کا جواب دیا ہے، اشاعرہ کا معارضہ اور معتزلہ کے جواب کی تنقر برزیل میں ملاحظہ ہو۔

معارضہ : اشاعرہ کہتے ہیں کہ حکم کو معطلی ماننے کی تقدیر پر بھی بعینہ اسی دلیل سے نبی کا انجام داسکات اور انکا عاجز و درماندہ ہونا لازم آتا ہے پس جو تمہارا جواب ہوگا وہ ہمارا بھی جواب ہوگا ۔ معارضہ یہ ہے که ثبوت و جوب نظر اگر چہ معتزلہ کے نزدیک عقلی ہے تا ہم وہ بد نہیں نہیں ہے بلکہ نظری ہے اور جب وجوب نظر نظری ہے تو معجزہ میں نظر کا حکم دیتے وقت نبی سے مکلف کہہ سکتا ہے کہ ہم معجزہ کو نہیں دیکھیں گے یہاں تک کہ وجوب نظر کو ثابت کر دیا جائے اور وجوب نظر ثابت نہیں ہو گا جب تک ہم نظر میں نظر نہ کریں گے پس اس وقت بھی ثبوت نظر موقوف ہو گیا ثبوت و جوب نظر پر اور ثبوت وجوب نظر موقوف ہوا ثبوت نظر فی انظر پر تو اس طرح ثبوت نظر موقوف ہو گیا ثبوت نظر پر اور یہ دور ہے جس کے دفع کی نبی کو راہ نہیں اس لئے نبی کا اسکات لازم آئے گا۔

جواب :۔ میں معتزلہ کہتے ہیں کہ انجام رسول کا اعتراض ہم پر نہیں پڑے گا کیونکہ دلیل مذکور کا مقدمہ لا يجب النظر عالم انظر کو ہم منع کرتے ہیں اسلئے کہ معجزات میں نظر کا وجوب ہمارے نزدیک شرع پر موقوف نہیں ہے بلکہ وہ قضایا نظریہ جلیہ بدیہیہ میں سے ہے جس کو فطر یہ القیاس کہتے ہیں چنانچہ قضیہ فطریۃ القیاس اس کو کہتے ہیں جس میں ایسا واسطہ پایا جاتا ہے جو ذہن سے بالکل غائب نہیں ہوتا ہے، ایسے قضایا کو قیا سا تھا معھا " سے بھی تعبیر کرتے ہیں جیسے الا ربعہ زوج چنانچہ جس نے اربعہ کا تصور کیا اور زوج کے مفہوم کا تصور کرے کہ زوج وہ ہے جو دو برابر حصہ میں بٹ جائے تو وہ بداہتہ حکم لگا دے گا کہ اربعہ زوج ہے اور جیسے ہمارا قول الواحد نصف الاثنین ، پس جو کوئی نصف الاثنین اور الواحد کا معنی و مفہوم جانتا ہے تو اس کی عقل بالبدالبتہ حکم لگا دیتی ہے کہ واحد، اثنین کا نصف ہے اس طرح معجزات میں نظر کا وجوب ہمارے نزدیک شرعی نہیں ہے بلکہ ایسا فطر یہ بدیہیہ ہے کہ بغیر استعانت شرع عقل وجوب نظر فی المعجزات کو جان لیتی ہے لہذا اس صورت میں رسول مکلف کو اگر کہیں کہ میرے معجزہ
He said, 'They said firstly: If the ruling were shar'i, it would necessitate...' The above passage mentions the Mu'tazila's first argument for ruling being rational. Before understanding this argument, keep these points in mind. It is known that obligation, prohibition, etc. are among the rulings, and ruling is the name of divine address. Divine address descends in the form of revelation upon the Prophet. Then the Prophet's prophethood is established by a miracle. So in the view of the obligated persons, the proof and manifestation of the Prophet's prophethood occurs by looking at the miracle that issued from the Prophet. In short, the proof of shar'i rulings like obligation depends on the proof of the Prophet's prophethood, because the rulings reach the servants through the Prophet. And in the view of the servants, the Prophet's prophethood is established only when the servants look at the Prophet's miracle. That is, the proof of the Prophet's prophethood depends on their looking at his miracle. Now listen to the Mu'tazila's argument! Summary of first argument: If the ruling is shar'i as the Ash'arites and Hanafis say - i.e., if the ruling is proven by the Prophet's prophethood or by the Shari'a - then the silencing and confounding of the Prophet would be necessary, and he would become unable and helpless to prove his prophethood and messengership. That is, when the Prophet displays a miracle to prove his claim of prophethood and commands the obligated people: 'Look at my miracle of prophethood so that you may verify my claim,' then the obligated people can say: 'We will not look at your miracle, because looking at the miracle is not obligatory upon us. And the obligation of looking at the miracle will not be proven without us looking at the miracle, because the obligation of looking is a ruling, and a ruling is proven by the statement of a person whose prophethood has been supported by a miracle. So his statement is true and his command is a definitive obligatory command. But at the time of commanding to look at the miracle, since prophethood has not yet been proven, his command will not be at the level of obligation. So when looking at the miracle is not obligatory, and the deniers did not look at the miracle, rather they refused to look, then prophethood was not proven. Instead, the Prophet is rendered helpless and compelled. Because in this case, the obligation of looking at the miracle depends on the proof of Shari'a or the proof of prophethood, and the proof of Shari'a and prophethood depends on looking at the miracle. So the obligation of looking at the miracle becomes dependent on looking at the miracle, and since looking at the miracle depends on the obligation of looking at the miracle, the obligation of looking at the miracle becomes dependent on the obligation of looking at the miracle. This is a vicious circle which the Prophet has no way to break if the ruling is shar'i. Therefore, his helplessness necessarily follows.

He said: 'They said: It does not apply to us, because the obligation of looking according to us...' The Ash'arites made an objection to the mentioned Mu'tazila argument. In the above passage, the Mu'tazila answer the Ash'arites' objection. The Ash'arites' objection and the Mu'tazila's response are noted in detail. Objection: The Ash'arites say that even on the assumption that the ruling is rational, exactly the same argument leads to the silencing and helplessness of the Prophet. So whatever answer you give will also be our answer. The objection is that although the proof of the obligation of looking is rational according to the Mu'tazila, it is not self-evident (badihi) but theoretical (nazari). And when the obligation of looking is theoretical, then at the time of commanding to look at the miracle, the obligated person can say: 'We will not look at the miracle until the obligation of looking is proven. And the obligation of looking will not be proven until we look at looking (nazar fi al-nazar).' So then the proof of looking depends on the proof of the obligation of looking, and the proof of the obligation of looking depends on the proof of looking at looking. Thus the proof of looking depends on the proof of looking, and this is a vicious circle which the Prophet has no way to break, so his silencing necessarily follows.

Answer: The Mu'tazila say that this objection against the Messenger will not apply to us, because we deny the premise of the mentioned argument, i.e., 'looking is not obligatory before looking' (la yajib al-nazar qabl al-nazar). This is because the obligation of looking at miracles in our view does not depend on Shari'a, but rather it is among the clear theoretical propositions that are self-evident (badihiyya), which are called 'fitri al-qiyas' (innate analogical). A proposition of fitri al-qiyas is that in which there is an intermediary that is not completely absent from the mind. Such propositions are also expressed as 'qiyas ma'ahu' (analogy with it). For example, 'four is even'. Whoever conceptualizes 'four' and conceptualizes the meaning of 'even' - that it is divisible into two equal parts - will immediately judge that four is even. And like our statement 'one is half of two'. So whoever knows the meaning and concept of 'half of two' and 'one', his intellect immediately judges that one is half of two. Similarly, the obligation of looking at miracles in our view is not shar'i, but rather it is such an innate self-evident matter that without the assistance of Shari'a, the intellect recognizes the obligation of looking at miracles. Therefore, in this case, if the Messenger says to the obligated person: 'Look at my miracle...'
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage is a dispute in usul al-fiqh between the Mu'tazila and the Ash'arites/Hanafis regarding the nature of hukm (ruling). The Mu'tazila argue that if rulings are shar'i (derived from Shari'a), it leads to a vicious circle in establishing prophethood. Their reasoning is that to know the Prophet's prophethood, one must look at his miracle, but looking at the miracle is only obligatory if the Prophet's command has authority, which itself depends on prophethood. Thus, they claim that rulings must be rational (aqli) to avoid this circle. The Ash'arites respond that even on the Mu'tazila's view, if the obligation to look is rational but theoretical (nazari), the same circularity arises because one must first know the obligation of looking before actually looking. The Mu'tazila counter that the obligation to look at miracles is a self-evident rational proposition (fitri al-qiyas) that does not require prior proof; like knowing that four is even or one is half of two, the intellect immediately recognizes the obligation to look at a miracle when presented. Therefore, they avoid the circularity. The Hanafi position, as an Ash'ari-adjacent school, holds that rulings are shar'i, but the necessity of looking at miracles is a rational necessity (badihi) that does not require prior Shari'a, thus the circle is broken. This passage illustrates the nuanced debate over the epistemological foundations of fiqh.

Key Terms
حکم شرعی (hukm shar'i): A ruling derived from divine revelation (Shari'a) via the Prophet, as opposed to rational deduction.
وجوب نظر فی المعجز (wujub al-nazar fi al-mu'jiz): The obligation to look at the Prophet's miracle in order to verify his prophethood.
قضیہ فطریۃ القیاس (qadiyya fitriyyat al-qiyas): A proposition that is self-evident through innate reasoning, where the middle term is not absent from the mind (e.g., 'four is even').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main premise of the Mu'tazila's first argument against hukm being shar'i?
A) If hukm is shar'i, then the obligation to look at a miracle depends on prophethood, and prophethood depends on looking, leading to a circle.
B) If hukm is shar'i, then the Prophet would be unable to perform miracles.
C) If hukm is shar'i, then there would be no need for reason.
D) If hukm is shar'i, then the Prophet would be obligated to obey the people.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi resolution to the circularity argument affirms that the duty to verify a prophet's miracle is a rational self-evident necessity, allowing hukm to remain shar'i without logical inconsistency.

Is Gratitude to God Rationally Obligatory? The Hanafi-Mu'tazila Dispute
Analyzing the matn on shukr al-mun'im and the dispute with Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school denies rational obligation of gratitude and evaluate the Mu'tazila counter-argument.

Core Idea
Gratitude to God is not rationally obligatory; it is known only through revelation.

This passage from Muslim al-Thubut addresses a foundational usul dispute: does reason alone make gratitude to God obligatory? The Hanafi school says no, contrary to the Mu'tazila. We'll examine the arguments and counterarguments, including the concessive framing (tanazzul) and the role of reason in ethical obligation.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its proof
Identify the matn's claim: gratitude is not rationally obligatory. The proof given: obligation requires benefit, but God gains none and man gains hardship in this world, and reason cannot assess the afterlife.
Hanafi position is built on rejecting rational obligation (tahsin wa taqbih 'aqli).
2
State the Mu'tazila position and their proof
The Mu'tazila argue that gratitude is rationally necessary (wajib 'aqli). Their proof: leaving gratitude risks punishment, and anything that secures from punishment is obligatory.
Mu'tazila accept rational obligation as a basis for ethics.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Mu'tazila
The Hanafi response counters two objections. First, the Mu'tazila compare gratitude to taking property without permission; the reply is that rational permission exists, like seeking shade. Second, the Mu'tazila claim gratitude without revelation resembles mockery; the reply is that sincerity matters, not form.
The Hanafi response undermines the rational necessity claim by highlighting the role of intention (ikhlas).
4
Identify the methodological issue: tanazzul (concession)
The matn begins with 'ala al-tanazzul (on the basis of concession). This means the Hanafi argument is presented even after granting the Mu'tazila premise that reason can know good and bad. Yet still the Hanafi concludes no rational obligation.
This shows strong confidence in the Hanafi position even on opposing assumptions.
5
Draw the practical thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if gratitude were rationally obligatory, a person who never received revelation would still be obliged to believe and thank God. The Hanafi view holds that such a person is not accountable until revelation comes.
This highlights the importance of revelation in determining obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متن المسلم : "مسألة على التنزيل شكر المنعم ليس بواجب عقلا خلافاً للمعتزلة واستدل بانه لو وجب لوجب بفائدة ولا فائدة له تعالى لتعاليه عنها ولا للعبد اما فى الدنيا فلانه مشقة واما فى الآخرة فلانه لا مجال للعقل في ذلك اقول بعد تسليم ما ادعاه المعتزلة كماهو معنى التنزل القول بانه لامجال للعقل مشكل على انه لوتم هذا لاستلزم عدم الوجوب مطلقا والظاهر أن الكلام في الخاص بعد تسليم المطلق مع أن المشقة لاينفى الفائدة فان العطايا على متن البلايا قال الله تعالى " والذين جاهدوا فينا لنهدينهم سبلنا قالوا انه يستلزم الامن من احتمال العقاب بتركه و كل ماكان كذلك فهو واجب . وعورض اولاً بانه تصرف فى ملك الغير بغير اذنه ويجاب بل بالاذن العقلى على أنه مثل الاستظلال والاستصباح وثانيا بانه يشبه الاستهزاء كيف وهو ضعيف فان المعتبر عند الله تعالى الاخلاص وايضا كيف يقال أن الشرع ورد بوجوب ما يشبه الاستهزاء فتدبر ترجمه :- (اشعریہ) نے علی سبیل التسليم معتزلہ کے برخلاف (کہا) کہ عقلی طور پر شکر منعم واجب
Matn from Muslim: "Issue: On the basis of concession (tanazzul), gratitude to the Benefactor is not rationally obligatory, contrary to the Mu'tazila. He argued: If it were obligatory, then it would be obligatory due to some benefit. But there is no benefit for Him (God), as He is transcendent above it; nor for the slave—in this world, because it is hardship; in the Hereafter, because reason has no scope in that. I say: After granting what the Mu'tazila claimed—as is the meaning of tanazzul—the statement that reason has no scope is problematic. Because if this were established, it would entail the non-obligation of anything absolutely? It seems that the discussion is about the specific after granting the general. Moreover, hardship does not negate benefit, for gifts come in the face of calamities. Allah said: 'And those who strive in Us, We will surely guide them to Our ways.' They said (the Mu'tazila argued): This entails security from the possibility of punishment for leaving it, and everything that is so is obligatory. It is objected, first, that it is a disposal in another's property without permission. And it is answered that it is by rational permission, like seeking shade and seeking light. And second, that it resembles mockery. How is that? And it is weak, because what is considered by Allah is sincerity. Also, how can it be said that the Law has come with obligation of what resembles mockery? So ponder. Translation: The Ash'ari, on the basis of concession (taslim), said contrary to the Mu'tazila that rationally, gratitude to the Benefactor is wajib."
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage presents a matn from Muslim al-Thubut discussing the issue of shukr al-mun'im (gratitude to the Benefactor). The matn states, in a concessive manner (tanazzul), that gratitude to God is not rationally obligatory, contrary to the Mu'tazila who hold it is rationally wajib. The argument given: if it were obligatory, it would have to be for a benefit (fā’ida). There is no benefit for God (He is self-sufficient) nor for the servant—in this world it is hardship, and in the afterlife reason has no say. The commentator then critiques this: after granting the Mu'tazila's claim that reason has no role in the afterlife, the argument is problematic because it would lead to no obligation at all. The discussion includes counterarguments from the Mu'tazila: gratitude is like taking a gift from someone else's property without permission; the response is that it is rationally permitted like seeking shade. Another counterargument is that it resembles mockery; this is weak because sincerity is what matters. The final Urdu translation seems to state the opposite: that the Ash'ari say gratitude is rationally wajib. This appears to be a summary of the matn's position (the Hanafi view) or perhaps a misprint; the Arabic matn clearly denies rational obligation. The passage ends with 'تدبر' (ponder).

Key Terms
شکر المنعم (shukr al-mun'im): Gratitude to the Benefactor (God), including acts of worship and thankfulness.
وجوب عقلی (wujūb 'aqlī): Obligation based on reason alone, without revelation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn from Muslim al-Thubut, is gratitude to the Benefactor rationally obligatory?
A) Yes, it is rationally wajib.
B) No, it is not rationally wajib.
C) It is wajib only for the Mu'tazila.
D) It is rationally wajib but not Shar'i.

Key Takeaway
Gratitude to God is a Shar'i obligation, not a rational one; reason alone cannot impose duties.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
