Mu'tazilah's Three Views on Pre-Shar'i Actions
متن المسلم: تقسيم المعتزلة للأفعال الاختيارية وأقوالهم الثلاثة قبل الشرع

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three Mu'tazilite positions on pre-shar'i actions and evaluate the logical critique of rational ibaha and hazr.

Core Idea
Before revelation, reason alone cannot assign rulings—Mu'tazilah's three views reveal the tension between rational judgment and divine law.

This lesson examines the Mu'tazilite classification of optional actions and their three competing stances on the status of such actions before divine revelation. The Hanafi school holds that the default is permissibility (ibaha) from the Law, while the Mu'tazilah divided into those claiming rational permissibility, rational prohibition, or suspension of judgment. The text also presents a critical argument: claiming both rational ibaha and hazr leads to contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Define optional actions and the two categories
Identify the scope of optional actions (al-af'al al-ikhtiyariyya) as those whose performance or omission does not threaten survival, e.g., eating fruit. Note that the Mu'tazilah split these into those where reason perceives husn/qubh and those where it does not.
The second category is the focus of the dispute.
2
Identify the three Mu'tazilite positions
List the three views: (1) rational permissibility (ibaha), (2) rational prohibition (hazr), and (3) suspension (tawaqquf). Understand the motivation behind each.
Each view is defended with a rational argument.
3
Examine the arguments for ibaha and hazr
Ibaha is argued to realize divine wisdom and avoid futility; hazr is argued to prevent unauthorized disposal of another's property. Recognize that both claim a rational basis for ruling.
These arguments rely on reason's ability to infer a ruling.
4
Understand the critique of both ibaha and hazr
The author objects that simultaneously positing both rational permissibility and prohibition assigns contradictory rulings to the same act. The defense using general vs. detailed knowledge does not remove the contradiction because differing causes do not resolve the logical conflict.
This critique undermines the rational foundation of both positions.
5
Evaluate the tawaqquf position
Tawaqquf holds that a specific ruling exists among the five, but it is unknown. The author notes that this suspension in the particular does not negate general knowledge of the ruling's existence.
Unlike ibaha and hazr, tawaqquf avoids contradiction by not assigning a concrete ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متن المسلم : "واما المعتزلة فقسموا الافعال الاختيارية وهي التي يمكن البقاء والتعيش بدونها كاكل الفاكهة مثلا الى ما يدرك فيه جهة محسنة او مقبحة فينقسم الى الاقسام الخمسة المشهورة والى ماليس كذالك ولهم فيه قبل الشرع ثلثة اقوال الاباحة تحصيلا لحكم الخلق دفعاً للعبث وربما يمنع الاستلزام والحظر لئلا يلزم التصرف فى ملك الغير بغير اذنه وقد مر ولا يرد عليهما انه كيف يقال بالاباحة والحظر العقليين وقد فرض ان لاحكم له فيه لان الفرض ان لاعلم بعلة الحكم تفصيلا ولا يمنع ذلك العلم اجمالا اقول يرد عليهما انه يلزم جواز اتصاف فعل بحكمين متضادين فى نفس الامر ولا ينفع الاجمال والتفصيل لان اختلاف العلة لا يرفع التناقض فتأمل ، الثالث التوقف لان ثمه حكما معينا من الخمسة ولا ادرى ايها واقع اقول هذا يقتضى الوقف في الخصوصية ولا يمنع ذلك العلم الاجمالي ، فتدبر"
ترجمه : ولیکن معتزلہ تو ان لوگوں نے افعال اختیاریہ اور وہ وہ ہے جس کے بغیر بقاء وتعیش ممکن ہو جیسے میوہ کھانا کی تقسیم کی ہے ان افعال کی طرف جس کے جہت حسن و قبیح کے طریق کو ادراک کیا جا سکے پس یہ پانچ اقسام مشہورہ کی طرف منقسم ہوتے ہیں ۔ اور ان افعال کی طرف جس کے حسن و قبح کے طریق کو اور اک نہ کیا جاسکے اور اس قسم میں قبل شرع معتزلہ کے تین اقوال ہیں (پہلا قول ) اباحت کا ہے تاکہ خلق اشیاء کی حکمتوں کو حاصل کر کے عبث سے بچا جا سکے اور بسا اوقات استلزام کو منع کیا جاتا ہے۔ ( دوسرا قول ) حظر وحرمت کا ہے تا کہ ملک غیر میں بلا اذن ما لک تصرف کرنا نہ لا زم آئے اور اس کی تفصیل گذر چکی ہے اور قول اباحت و قول حرمت پر یہ اعتراض وارد نہیں ہوگا کہ کیونکر اباحت عقلیہ اور حرمت عقلیہ کا قول کیا جاتا ہے جب کہ فرض یہ کیا گیا ہے کہ اس میں عقل کے نزدیک حکم نہیں ہے کیونکہ مفروض یہ ہے کہ حکم کی علت کا تفصیلی علم نہیں ہے اور یہ علم اجمالی کے منافی نہیں ہے میں کہتا ہوں کہ قول اباحت اور قول حظر پر ایک فعل کا دوحکم متضاد کے ساتھ نفس الامر میں انصاف کا جواز لازم آتا ہے اور اجمال و تفصیل نفع بخش نہ ہوگا کیونکہ علت کا اختلاف تناقض کو ختم نہیں کر سکتا اسی لئے غور کرو۔ تیسرا قول توقف کا ہے اس لئے کہ اس جگہ پانچوں احکام میں سے ایک حکم متعین ہے اور یہ نہیں معلوم کہ ان پانچوں سے کون واقع ہے، میں کہوں گا کہ یہ وقف فی الخصوصیت کو چاہتا ہے اور یہ علم اجمالی کے منافی نہیں ہے لہذا غور کرو؟
The matn of al-Muslim: "As for the Mu'tazilah, they divided optional actions — those which life and livelihood can do without, like eating fruit, for example — into [those] in which a good or bad aspect is perceived, so it divides into the five well-known categories, and [those] which are not like that. And regarding them before the [arrival of] the Law, they have three sayings: permissibility, in order to attain the wisdom of creation and avoid futility, and sometimes [they] prevent the implication; and prohibition, so that disposal of another's property without his permission is not necessitated, and it has passed. And the objection that how can rational permissibility and prohibition be said while it is assumed that there is no ruling for it [rationally] does not apply to these two, because the assumption is that there is no detailed knowledge of the cause of the ruling, and that does not prevent general knowledge. I say: an objection applies to them, that it necessitates the permissibility of an act being described by two contradictory rulings in the same real entity, and the general and detailed [knowledge] does not benefit, because difference of cause does not remove contradiction, so reflect. The third: suspension, because there is a specific ruling among the five and I do not know which one occurs. I say: this necessitates suspension in the particular, and that does not prevent general knowledge, so ponder."
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage presents the Mu'tazilite position on the status of human actions before revelation (qabl al-shar'), a key usul al-fiqh dispute. The matn first defines optional actions (al-af'al al-ikhtiyariyya) as those whose existence is not necessary for life, e.g., eating fruit for pleasure. The Mu'tazilah then split these actions into two categories: (1) those where reason can perceive a good (husn) or bad (qubh) aspect—these fall into the five well-known categories (wajib, haram, makruh, mandub, mubah); (2) those where reason cannot perceive such an aspect. For the second category, before revelation (qabl al-shar'), the Mu'tazilah have three opinions. The first is ibaha (permissibility), argued to realize divine wisdom and avoid futility. The second is hazr (prohibition), to avoid unauthorized disposal of another's property. The author critiques both: claiming rational permissibility and prohibition both simultaneously assigns contradictory rulings to the same act, and using general vs. detailed knowledge does not resolve the logical contradiction. The third opinion is tawaqquf (suspension), maintaining that a specific ruling exists but is unknown. The author notes that this suspension in the particular is compatible with general knowledge of the ruling's existence. This discussion is foundational for understanding the Hanafi view that before revelation, the default ruling in actions is ibaha, as opposed to the Mu'tazilite hazr view.

Key Terms
الافعال الاختيارية (al-af'al al-ikhtiyariyya): Actions whose performance or omission does not threaten survival, such as eating fruit for pleasure.
قبل الشرع (qabl al-shar'): The period before the revelation of divine law; actions are not yet subject to revealed rulings.
الاباحة العقلية (al-ibaha al-'aqliyya): Rational permissibility: the judgment by reason that an act is allowed, as claimed by some Mu'tazilah.
الحظر العقلي (al-hazr al-'aqli): Rational prohibition: the judgment by reason that an act is forbidden, as claimed by other Mu'tazilah.
التوقف (al-tawaqquf): Suspension of judgment: neither affirming permissibility nor prohibition, because the true ruling is unknown.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazilah, regarding optional actions before revelation, which of the following is NOT one of their three opinions?
A) Ibaha
B) Hazr
C) Tawaqquf
D) Istihsan

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilah had three competing rational positions on pre-shar'i actions, but the Hanafi school holds that permissibility before revelation is established by the Law, avoiding the logical contradictions inherent in rational ibaha and hazr.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Mu'tazilite Rational Taxonomy of Legal Categories
Mu'tazilite rational taxonomy of action categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Mu'tazilite rational categories of wajib, haram, makruh, mandub, and mubah, and explain how they derive them from perceived good and bad aspects, while distinguishing this from the Hanafi requirement of revelation.

Core Idea
Mu'tazilah derive five legal categories from reason alone; Hanafis require revelation.

In the previous discussion, the disagreement among non-Mu'tazilite scholars on the ruling of actions before revelation was presented. Now the author turns to the Mu'tazilah, who claim that reason alone can generate a complete moral taxonomy. This lesson unpacks their division of optional actions (al-af‘al al-ikhtiyāriyya) into five categories based on the strength of the perceived good or bad aspect, and contrasts it with the Hanafi insistence that such rulings require divine texts.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish optional from non-optional actions
According to the Mu'tazilah, before revelation, human actions are split into optional (those dispensable for survival, like recreational fruit-eating) and non-optional. The five categories only apply to the optional ones.
Non-optional actions (e.g., breathing) have no rational moral evaluation.
2
Identify which optional actions have perceptible good/bad
Within optional actions, some have a good or bad aspect that reason can perceive; others do not. The five categories are only for those with perceptible aspects.
For actions with imperceptible aspects, Mu'tazilah hold differing opinions: ibaha, hazr, or tawaqquf.
3
Map the five categories based on strength of aspect
Reason perceives a strong good aspect → wajib (omission blameworthy). Strong bad → haram (commission punishable). Weak bad → makruh (omission preferable). Weak good → mandub (commission rewardable). Neither aspect → mubah.
The categories are derived from the intensity of the good/bad perceived by reason, not from revelation.
4
Contrast with Hanafi view
Hanafis reject that reason alone can determine moral categories. Without revelation, actions before revelation are either mubah (permissible) or subject to tawaqquf (suspension). The Mu'tazilite rational taxonomy is considered invalid without shar‘i texts.
This is a key usul al-fiqh dispute: can reason generate hukm without revelation?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشريح : گذشتہ سطور میں فرقہ معتزلہ کے علاوہ علماء حق کے مابین اشیاء کی اباحت وحرمت کے بارے میں اختلاف کا ذکر تھا کہ بعض وہ افعال جس میں شرع وارد نہیں ہے یا ورود شرع کے پہلے افعال کا حکم اہل اباحت کے نزدیک مباح ہے اور اہل نظر کے نزدیک ممنوع ہے، اب مصنف نے اسباب میں معتزلہ کے موقف اور انکے مابین اختلاف کو ذکر کیا ہے جس کی تفصیل ذیل میں ملاحظہ ہو۔
قوله - اما المعتزلة فقسموا الافعال الاختيارية وهى الخ خیال رہے کہ معتزلہ کے نزدیک قبل ورود شرع بندہ کے افعال دو طرح کے کہلاتے ہیں، افعال اختیاریه، افعال غیر اختیاریه، افعال اختیار یہ وہ فعل کہلاتا ہے جس کے بغیر تعیش و بقا ممکن ہو جیسے اکل فواکہہ ان علاقوں میں جہاں بطور تفریح طبع فواکہ واثمار کا استعمال ہوتا ہے۔ اور افعال اختیار یہ کی دو قسمیں ہیں ایک وہ افعال اختیار یہ جس کے حسن و فتح کے طرق کو عقل اور اک کر لیتی ہے دوسری قسم وہ افعال اختیار یہ جس کے حسن و فتح کے طرق کو عقل ادراک نہیں کر سکتی ہے پھر قسم اول (یعنی جس میں جہت حسن و فتح کو بذریعہ عقل اور اک کیا جاسکتا ہے ) تو اس کی مشہور پانچ قسمیں ہیں، واجب، حرام، مکروہ ، مندوب اور مباح پس عقل نے فعل میں اگر جہت محسنہ قویہ کا ادراک کیا ایسا حسن قوی کہ اس کا ترک فتح اور ذم و عقاب کا باعث ہے تو وہ فعل واجب ہے اس کے برخلاف اگر جہت مقبحہ قویہ کا ادراک کیا ایسا فتح شدید کہ اسکا ارتکاب باعث عقاب اور ترک باعث اجر و ثواب ہے تو وہ حرام ہے۔ البتہ اگر عقل نے فتح ضعیف کا ادراک کیا ایسا ضعف کہ فعل باعث عقاب نہیں ہے لیکن اس کا ترک فعل کے بہ نسبت اولی ہے تو وہ مکروہ ہے اور اگر عقل نے جہت محسنہ ضعیفہ کا ادراک کیا ایسا حسن ضعیف کہ اسکا کرنا باعث ثواب ہے لیکن ترک سبب عقاب نہیں تو وہ مندوب ہے اور اگر فعل و ترک دونوں جہتیں ثواب و عقاب کی طرف مستدعی نہ ہونے میں مساوی ہیں تو وہ مباح ہے۔
Explanation: In the previous lines, apart from the Mu'tazila sect, the disagreement among the scholars of truth concerning the permissibility and prohibition of things was mentioned, that [for] some of those actions regarding which no law has come, or before the coming of law, the ruling according to the proponents of permissibility is permissible, and according to the people of consideration it is prohibited. Now the author has mentioned the stance of the Mu'tazila and the disagreement among them in this context, details of which are seen below. His saying: "As for the Mu'tazila, they divided the optional actions..." Keep in mind that according to the Mu'tazila, before the coming of law, a person's actions are of two types: optional actions and non-optional actions. An optional action is that which one can live without, like eating fruits in regions where fruits and crops are used for recreation. And optional actions are of two divisions: one is those optional actions whose path of good and bad reason perceives; the second is those optional actions whose path of good and bad reason cannot perceive. Then the first division (i.e., that in which the aspect of good and bad can be perceived by reason) has five famous categories: wajib, haram, makruh, mandub, and mubah. So if reason perceives in an act a strong good aspect, such strong good that its omission causes evil and blame and punishment, then that act is wajib. Contrary to that, if it perceives a strong bad aspect, such intense evil that committing it causes punishment and omitting it causes reward, then that is haram. However, if reason perceives a weak evil, such weakness that the act does not cause punishment but its omission is superior to the act, then it is makruh. And if reason perceives a weak good aspect, such weak good that doing it causes reward but omission does not cause punishment, then it is mandub. And if both doing and omitting are equal in not prompting reward or punishment, then it is mubah.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This commentary (tashrih) expands on the Mu'tazilite position by first contextualizing the earlier discussion: the dispute among non-Mu'tazilite 'scholars of truth' (ulama' haqq) about the ruling on actions before revelation. The author then clarifies the Mu'tazilite view. According to them, before revelation, human actions are either optional (ikhtiyari) or non-optional. Optional actions are those dispensable for life, like recreational fruit-eating. These are further split: some have a good or bad aspect perceptible by reason, others do not. For the latter, the three opinions (ibaha, hazr, tawaqquf) apply. The commentary then details the five rational categories for the former: wajib (strong good, omission blameworthy), haram (strong bad, act blameworthy), makruh (weak bad, omission preferable), mandub (weak good, act praiseworthy but omission not blameworthy), and mubah (equal). This demonstrates the Mu'tazilite claim that reason alone can generate a complete moral taxonomy, unlike the Hanafi view that such categories require divine revelation.

Key Terms
جہت محسنہ قویہ (jihat muhsina qawiyya): A strong good aspect perceived by reason that makes omission blameworthy and punishable.
جہت مقبحہ قویہ (jihat muqabbiha qawiyya): A strong bad aspect perceived by reason that makes commission punishable.
افعال اختیاریہ (af‘al ikhtiyariyya): Optional actions that one can live without, like recreational eating.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazilah, what is the difference between wajib and mandub in the pre-shar'i context?
A) Wajib has strong good aspect; mandub has weak good aspect.
B) Wajib has strong bad aspect; mandub has weak bad aspect.
C) Wajib is known by revelation; mandub by reason.
D) Wajib requires punishment for omission; mandub requires punishment for commission.

Key Takeaway
Mu'tazilah categorize optional actions into five rational categories based on perceived good/bad strength; Hanafis reject this without revelation.
